ATTACHMENT 4:          Past Performance Evaluation Questionnaire


BACKGROUND:

The U.S. Census Bureau (Census Bureau) serves as the leading source of quality data about the nation's  people  and  economy.  The  role  of  the
Census Bureau’s Public Information Office (PIO) is to gain positive coverage of Census Bureau programs, people and products.  The  PIO  offers  a
variety of services to help publicize Census Bureau materials (data releases, media  advisories,  photos,  daily  features,  events,  statistical
releases, products and services).  PIO requires the ability to distribute materials through a newswire distribution subscription system  to  news
organizations in support of the Census Bureau decennial census, American Community Survey, Economic data programs, and other  census  and  survey
programs.

The information hereby requested is intended to assist the U.S. Census Bureau to  assess  the  effectiveness  and  performance  of  the  product/
contractor identified below.

INSTRUCTIONS:

standards shall be used in arriving at the rating.

  (O) - Outstanding    Contractor’s performance/ Service exceeded customer expectations and was technically acceptable, providing significant
                 features or benefits.


  (S) - Satisfactory   Contractor/ Service  met customer expectations or contract requirements and demonstrated an acceptable understanding of
                 the requirements.


  (U) - Unsatisfactory   Contractor’s performance / Service was either marginal or did not meet customer expectations or contract requirements.


  N/A       Element is not applicable.  If no data has been obtained, please note in this column.

Census Bureau IT Security Policies

1.0 INTRODUCTION
The U.S. Census Bureau is strongly committed to Information Technology (IT) Security. Census Bureau senior leaders recognize that security must be inherent in our business processes and IT systems. Census Bureau managers systematically recognize and address information security risks and take steps to understand and manage these risks. This is important, not only to achieve compliance with public laws, federal regulations, and standards, but also to aid in the Census Bureau mission to foster, promote, and develop the foreign and domestic commerce of the United States. This document sets forth the Census Bureau IT Security Program Policies and is consistent with the Department of Commerce IT Security Program Policy (DOC ITSPP).

1.1

BACKGROUND

The Census Bureau's mission is to serve as the leading source of quality data about the Nation's people and economy. Because of the nature of this mission, protecting information and the systems that collect, process, and maintain that information is of critical importance. Therefore, securing information resources must include controls and safeguards to offset possible threats, as well as controls to ensure data confidentiality, integrity, and availability. Provisions of the Privacy Act and United States Code Title 13 protect much of the data collected by the Census Bureau and make releasing sensitive data covered under these provisions a criminal act punishable by federal law. The Census Bureau strives to ensure that data confidentiality and integrity are consistent with statutory requirements and ethical considerations, while meeting the need for availability. Information security supports the Census Bureau mission by ensuring our information and systems are protected against risks of loss, misuse, or unauthorized access in accordance with applicable laws.

1.2

PURPOSE

The Census Bureau IT Security Program Policies specifies the mandatory requirements for the Census Bureau IT Security Program, which encompasses controls to be implemented on information and systems. This policy addresses requirements and guidance set forth by the Federal Information Security Management Act (FISMA) and provides clarity on the Department of Commerce and Census Bureau's specific parameters. It also encompasses minimum security controls as required by Federal Information Processing Standard (FIPS) 200, Minimum Security Requirements for Federal Information and Information Systems, and defined by National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) Special Publication (SP) 800-53, Revision 3, Recommended Security Controls for Federal Information Systems, commensurate with the security categorization defined by FIPS 199, Standards for Security Categorization of Federal Information and Information Systems.

1.3

SCOPE

This policy applies to all non-public users of Census Bureau IT and all IT systems owned or operated on behalf of the Census Bureau. Requirements contained herein apply also to systems that are not owned by the Census Bureau but to which the Census Bureau interconnects and has legal and/or contractual authority to dictate requirements. The policies defined and discussed in this document apply to all Census Bureau divisions and offices and their employees (federal and
1 For Official Use Only

Census Bureau IT Security Policies

April 2010

contractors), guest researchers, collaborators, and other personnel requiring access to the hardware and software components that constitute the Census Bureau's IT information systems. Classified information and systems are not within the scope of this document.

1.4

CENSUS BUREAU IT SECURITY PROGRAM DOCUMENTATION

This policy encompasses the DOC ITSPP. Additional requirements are contained in the Commerce Interim Technical Requirements (CITRs), NIST Standard Publications, and Census Bureau supporting security program policies, procedures and guidelines support. This policy includes policy statements, security control parameters and criteria. The statements and parameters are in concert with NIST SP 800-53, Revision 3 and include criteria when specificity is warranted. The parameters and criteria are mapped to a subset of required controls, which shall be instituted to fully implement the control. When parameters are not provided in this policy, Program Area (OU) IT security personnel shall develop organization-defined parameters for their respective environment. The CITRs are released as new mandates require the implementation of additional IT security measures. The CITRs are real-time updates that append or supersede the current version of the DOC ITSPP and this policy. The CITRs must be reviewed and approved by the DOC Chief Information Officer (CIO) Council and carry authority equal to the DOC ITSPP and hence this policy. This document is divided into four (4) sections: Section 1, Introduction, describes the background, purpose, scope, and documentation. Section 2, Policy, describes the policy authority, effective date, waivers, and enforcement. Section 3, IT Security Roles and Responsibilities, provides an outline of the departmental offices, roles, and IT groups. Section 4, Baseline Security Controls, contain a complete list of security controls with DOC and/or Census Bureau specific criteria. A listing of acronyms, terms, references, offices can be found in the appendices. This policy and related documents can be found on the Census Bureau Intranet (http://cww.census.gov/it/itso/AV_itso_SecPubPol.asp) and the DOC ITSPP and CITRs can be found on the DOC Intranet (http://home.commerce.gov/CIO/ITSITnew/default.html). Comments or questions regarding this policy can be submitted via e-mail to IT.Security.Chief@census.gov.

2 For Official Use Only

Census Bureau IT Security Policies

April 2010

2.0 POLICY
The Census Bureau shall develop, document, and implement an IT Security Program to protect the confidentiality, integrity, and availability of Census Bureau information and systems in accordance with the Federal Information Security Management Act (FISMA) of 2002 (Title III, Pub. L. No. 107-347). The Census Bureau shall use FIPS 199 to categorize information systems and determine their appropriate impact levels (Low, Moderate, High). The Census Bureau shall select the security controls baseline defined in NIST SP 800-53, Revision 3 based on the system's impact level, and tailor, supplement, and implement the baseline according to NIST 800-53. The Census Bureau shall use NIST SP 800-53A, Guide for Assessing the Security Controls in Federal Information Systems as the basis for assessing information system security controls to determine the extent to which they are implemented correctly, operating as intended, and producing the desired outcome with respect to meeting the security requirements. The Census Bureau shall certify and accredit information systems in accordance with NIST SP 800-37, Guide for the Security Certification and Accreditation of Federal Information Systems. The Census Bureau shall be compliant with revisions to the aforementioned documents within one year of issuance. The Census Bureau shall supplement these publications with this policy and DOC CITRs.

2.1

EFFECTIVE DATE

The 2010 BOC IT Security Program Policies is effective upon issuance and supersedes the 2009 BOC IT Security Program Policies and incorporates the requirements of the DOC ITSPP and the following CITRs, which will remain in effect until superseded by updated CITRs. CITR-001: Federal Desktop Core Configuration (FDCC) CITR-002: Safeguarding Data on Foreign Travel CITR-003: Continuous Monitoring CITR-004: DOC Certification & Accreditation (C&A) Process o Supplement 1 to CITR 004 (Released on July 21, 2009) o IT Investment Security Authorization Responsibilities o IT Security Roles and Responsibilities o DOC CSAM Working Group Memorandum CITR-005: Removable Media Devices CITR-008: Remote Access CITR-009: Password Requirements CITR-011: Peer-to-Peer Technology For information about all current CITRs, please visit the DOC IT Security Documentation website: http://home.commerce.gov/CIO/ITSITnew/IT_Security_Program_Documentation.html The updated DOC ITSPP and this policy supersedes the following security memorandums previously issued by DOC Senior Officials (e.g., Deputy Secretary): Safeguarding Personally Identifiable Information (PII) memorandum dated December 12, 2006. Safeguarding Personally Identifiable Information memorandum dated November 6, 2006.
3 For Official Use Only

Census Bureau IT Security Policies

April 2010

System Owners/Program Areas are required to comply with this policy within 120 days and CITRs within 90 days, or as stipulated in the CITR. Compliance with this policy and DOC CITR requirements beyond the specified timeframe shall be managed through the Plan of Action and Milestones (POA&Ms). The DOC Chief Information Security Officer (CISO)/Senior Agency Information Security Officer (SAISO) will review the DOC ITSPP and incorporate updates, including CITRs and new federal requirements, as required but at least biennially. The revised DOC ITSPP shall be reviewed and concurred by the CIO Council. Subsequent to this, the Census Bureau IT Security Office will incorporate the changes into this policy and the revision shall be reviewed and concurred by Census Bureau stakeholders.

2.2

SCOPING AND WAIVERS

System Owners/Program Areas have the flexibility to tailor security control baselines in accordance with the terms and conditions set forth in the Scoping Guidance section of NIST SP 800-53, Revision 3. Scoping provides specific terms and conditions on the applicability and implementation of NIST SP 800-53 security controls. In addition, scoping shall also be applied to controls and parameters that fall outside of the NIST SP 800-53 framework (e.g. DOC Criteria, Census Bureau Criteria) and for which waivers are not required by Census Bureau CIO. Questions regarding controls and parameters can be submitted to the Census Bureau ITSO/SAISO. The Authorizing Official (AO) shall approve the tailoring of security control baselines. For controls and parameters that require a waiver, requests shall be submitted to the Census Bureau CIO, through the Census Bureau ITSO/SAISO. In addition, the DOC CIO has the discretion to elevate the waiver approval process to the level of the Office of the CIO when actions or controls are identified that affect department-wide security. Waiver requests shall justify and describe the controls that cannot be fully implemented and the compensating controls in-place. Corrective action items shall be specified in the waiver requests, if appropriate. System Owners/Program Areas shall use the POA&Ms to track and manage progress towards compliance. The Census Bureau CIO shall respond to waiver requests within thirty (30) calendar days. Waiver responses shall include (i) approval and conditions for approval, including expiration date, if appropriate, (ii) denial and basis for the denial, or (iii) additional information requested. Upon request from the DOC CIO, the Census Bureau ITSO/SAISO shall verify the Departmentlevel waiver requirements and submit copies of waivers for the purpose of performing Department-wide trend analysis and enterprise risk management.

2.3

ENFORCEMENT

The DOC ITSPP, CITRs and this policy are issued under the authority of the Department Administrative Order (DAO) 200-0, DOC Handbooks and Manuals as a section of the IT Management Handbook, and thereby have the same force and effect of a DAO. Violations of these policies may result in losing IT access and/or disciplinary action, up to and including removal, consistent with DAO 202-751, Discipline, and/or civil or criminal action against the offending employee(s), associate(s), and/or contractor(s), consistent with law, or contract terms as applicable.
4 For Official Use Only

Census Bureau IT Security Policies

April 2010

3.0 IT SECURITY ROLES AND RESPONSIBILITIES
The responsibility to protect Census Bureau information and technological resources extends to all non-public users and requires collaboration across various offices to coordinate activities associated with the Census Bureau's security posture, technological environment and overall risk management.

3.1

PERSONNEL

The following guidelines apply to individuals with security responsibilities at the DOC: All of the responsibilities and requirements delineated by this policy apply to any individual performing the security role, regardless of employer. DOC and Census Bureau personnel should implement the practices and guidance found in Security Programs, DAO 207-1.

3.2

DEPARTMENTAL ROLES

The roles in this section are carried out by individuals at the Departmental-level. 3.2.1 Secretary of Commerce The Secretary of Commerce is responsible for ensuring the DOC information and technological resources are protected in accordance with directives from the Office of Management and Budget (OMB), Congress, and as set forth in Presidential Directives. The DOC Senior Officials are responsible for the day-to-day management and general supervision of their respective programs and/or OUs. 3.2.2 DOC Chief Information Officer (CIO) The responsibilities of the CIO are generally defined in NIST SP 800-37, and more specifically defined for the DOC CIO in Departmental Organization Order (DOO) 15-23, Chief Information Officer. The DOC CIO shall: Designate in writing a DOC SAISO to execute the IT Security Program for national and non-national security systems. Approve and issue DOC ITSPP and CITRs that establish a framework for an IT Security Program to be implemented by the DOC and its OUs; and, Monitor, evaluate, and report to the Secretary of Commerce on the status of IT security within the Department. 3.2.3 DOC Chief Information Security Officer (CISO)/ Senior Agency Information Security Officer (SAISO) The DOC CISO is the SAISO who directs the management of the Department's IT Security Program. The DOC CISO/SAISO, with the support of DOC Senior Officials, establishes a strong foundation for DOC IT security by interacting with internal and external resources, and
5 For Official Use Only

Census Bureau IT Security Policies

April 2010

coordinating IT security compliance across DOC organizational elements. The responsibilities of the CISO/SAISO are generally defined in NIST SP 800-37. The DOC CISO/SAISO shall coordinate with the DOC CIO, Director of the Office of IT Security, Infrastructure, and Technology (OITSIT), the Compliance and Risk Management Officer (CRMO), the Critical Infrastructure Protection Manager (CIPM) and OU CIOs to: Develop, document, and implement the DOC IT Security Program to provide information security for the electronic information and information systems that support the operations and assets of the DOC including those provided or managed by another agency, contractor, or other source, that includes: o Develop and maintain IT Security policies, plans, control techniques and procedures for information systems, to include developing related standards to be followed by the OU, and developing standards, procedures and practices to establish an IT Security Program as an integral part of the IT Management Program; o Inform personnel of training requirements (i.e. IT Security Awareness Training) to access information systems that support the operations and assets of the DOC; o Train and oversee personnel with significant responsibilities for information security with respect to such responsibilities; and, o Define activities associated with Certification and Accreditation (C&A), including configuration management, security assessment, and implementation of enterprise-wide tools. Plan and co-chair regular meetings of the IT Security Coordinating Committee (ITSCC) as a forum for exchange and action on Department-wide IT security policies. 3.2.4 DOC Director of the Office of IT Security, Infrastructure and Technology (OITSIT) The DOC Director of the OITSIT shall coordinate with the DOC CIO, CISO/SAISO, CRMO, CIPM and OU CIOs to: Ensure IT security is included in the DOC Strategic IT Planning and Enterprise Architecture (EA) efforts; Identify IT security resource requirements for the Department. Each OU CIO or equivalent will ensure that funds and personnel, needed to manage the IT Security Program are adequately addressed within their OU. 3.2.5 DOC IT Security Compliance & Risk Management Officer (CRMO) The DOC CRMO shall coordinate with the DOC CIO, CISO/SAISO, Director of OITSIT, CIPM and OU CIOs to: Monitor and evaluate the status of the DOC IT Security posture by performing annual compliance reviews of OU IT Security Programs; Advise the DOC CIO and OU CIOs of technological IT security advances that can be used on a Department-wide scale and provide reduced costs for IT security efforts; and Report to the DOC CIO and external entities, such as OMB, Government Accountability Office (GAO), and Congress, on IT Security Program status within the Department.

April 2010

3.2.6 DOC Critical Infrastructure Protection Manager (CIPM) The responsibilities of the DOC CIPM encompass establishment, coordination, and implementation of all activities associated with the protection of Critical Infrastructure, including the IT component of Continuity of Operations Planning (COOP). The CIPM shall coordinate with the DOC CIO, CISO/SAISO, Director of OITSIT, CRMO, CIPM and OU CIOs to: Develop the DOC Critical Infrastructure Protection (CIP) Program, including providing the Director of the OITSIT with input to policies and procedures for (i) incident response capability, (ii) the IT component of COOP; Act as the DOC liaison with U.S. Computer Emergency Readiness Team (US-CERT), and manage DOC Federated Computer Incident Response Program; and, Identify resource requirements, including funds, personnel, and contractors, needed to manage the CIP Program. 3.2.7 DOC Director for Security The DOC Director for Security, as defined by DOO 20-6, Section 5, Director for Security shall coordinate with the DOC CIO, CISO/SAISO, Director of OITSIT, CRMO, CIPM and OU CIOs to: Develop and enforce appropriate physical security controls; Identify and address the physical security needs of computer installations, office environments, and back-up installations; Process and maintain personal background checks and security clearance records; Issue Identification (ID) badges to DOC personnel at the Office of Security (OSY) controlled Credentialing Centers and Common Access Card (CAC) stations in accordance with Homeland Security Presidential Directive-12 (HSPD-12); Serve as the Department's liaison with agencies of federal, state, and local government in security, executive protection, and Departmental counterintelligence issues; and, Conduct investigations under the authorities, functions, and responsibilities of OSY. 3.2.8 DOC Privacy Officer The DOC CIO functions as the Department's Senior Official for Privacy (SAOP), consistent with the responsibilities under the E-Government Act of 2002, and FISMA. The DOC SAOP shall coordinate with the Privacy Act Officer, and the Department's Chief Financial Officer (CFO)/Assistant Secretary for Administration to: Ensure that confidentiality is addressed commensurate with privacy concerns of DOC information. Develop and evaluate legislative, regulatory, and policy proposals, which involve privacy issues.

3.3

OPERATING UNIT (CENSUS BUREAU) ROLES

The following roles are carried out by individuals in each of the Operating Units (OUs): 3.3.1 Director, Census Bureau The Director of the Census Bureau is accountable to the DOC for developing and implementing the Census Bureau's IT security program and delegates the following responsibilities to the Census Bureau CIO: Communicate the importance of IT security in the Census Bureau's mission to all Census Bureau employees. Assign management of IT systems to responsible program officials (e.g., heads of line offices and major Census Bureau components). Ensure that the Census Bureau has an established IT security program to protect its IT systems. Serve as, or delegates to another senior management official (at the Associate Director level), the AO for IT systems that support the Census Bureau's mission. Ensure, in consultation with the Office of Human Resource Management, that each position is designated at the appropriate level of sensitivity and/or risk in accordance with the DOC Security Manual, Chapter 10. They shall also ensure that this designation is clearly stated in the position description so that the Office of Security (OSY) can perform the appropriate background investigation. 3.3.2 OU Chief Information Officer (CIO) OU CIOs shall examine the interdependencies and interconnections of IT resources and provide for the separation of duties, including sufficient supervision and coordination among System Owners (SOs). The responsibilities of the CIO are generally defined in NIST SP 800-37. The OU CIO shall coordinate with the DOC CIO, CISO/SAISO, Director of OITSIT, CRMO, CIPM and OU ITSO/SAISO to: Manage the OU IT Security Program and approval of OU supplements to the DOC ITSPP; Develop, maintain, and oversee the OU IT Security Policy; Ensure that IT security policies are developed and approved; Appoint, in writing, an OU ITSO/SAISO to implement the IT Security Program; Ensure the implementation of the IT Security Program complies with FISMA, which includes independent evaluations of the program; Provide overall management of and leadership and direction to the IT Security Program; Report the status of the IT Security Program to the DOC CRMO, and any weaknesses of the program; Ensure that the IT Security Planning is done throughout the life cycle of the system; Ensuring that all IT resources are identified, including complying with the Department's capital asset budget planning process, and following a methodology consistent with NIST SP 800-65, Integrating IT Security into the Capital Planning and Capital Investment Control Process, and making IT security explicit in IT investments and capital program; Train and oversee personnel with significant responsibilities for information security;

8 For Official Use Only

Census Bureau IT Security Policies

April 2010

Provide feedback to the Department on the status of the program in the OU as required by FISMA, and suggest improvements or areas of concern in the OU program or any other Departmental program or activity; and, Serve as the Authorizing Official (AO) or Co-AO, as necessary, for unclassified systems within the OU. 3.3.3 OU Privacy Act Officer/Freedom of Information Act (FOIA) Officer Each OU Privacy Officer/FOIA Officer or equivalent is responsible for providing information on procedural issues involving the Privacy Act and addressing privacy concerns relative to their individual OU. The Office of General Counsel (OGC) provides guidance on all legal issues involving the Privacy Act. 3.3.4 OU IT Security Officer (ITSO)/SAISO The OU ITSO is the SAISO appointed by the OU CIO. An OU ITSO/SAISO is responsible for ensuring the appropriate operational security posture is maintained for information systems and programs under their OU's control. The OU ITSO/SAISO reports to the DOC CISO/SAISO, through the OU CIO. The OU ITSO/SAISO serves as the principal advisor to the AO, SO, and DOC CISO/SAISO on all matters (technical and otherwise) involving the security of the OU's IT systems, and maintains a copy of each Security Accreditation Package (SAP) for use in performing required IT security monitoring and reporting responsibilities. Additionally, the OU ITSO/SAISO shall: Develop and maintain the OU IT Security Policy, procedures, standards, and guidance consistent with Departmental and Federal requirements; Conduct continuous monitoring of the OU's IT Security Program annually to ensure effective implementation of, and compliance with, established policies and procedures; Establish a process to ensure that all users are provided with periodic security awareness briefings, copies of Rules of Behavior (RoB), and are trained to fulfill their IT security responsibilities including procedures for general and specialized training; Notify SOs of user infractions identified during routine compliance assessments; Participate as a voting member of the ITSCC, participate in special committees under the ITSCC, and provide other support for the ITSCC as appropriate; and, Coordinate with the Director of the OITSIT, OU CIO and CIPM, as appropriate, concerning incidents and potential threats. 3.3.5 Authorizing Official (AO) The responsibilities of the AO are generally defined in NIST SP 800-37. The AO must have the authority to oversee the budget and business operations of the information system within the OU. The AO has the authority to assume responsibility for operating an information system at an acceptable level of risk to operations, assets, or individuals by granting an Authorization to Operate (ATO), Interim Authorization to Operate (IATO) or Denial of Authority to Operate (DATO) as defined in NIST SP 800-37. The AO shall authorize system security requirements, System Security Plans (SSPs), Interconnection System Agreements (ISAs), and Memorandum of Agreements (MOAs) and/or Memorandum of Understandings (MOUs).

9 For Official Use Only

Census Bureau IT Security Policies

April 2010

With the increasing complexities of missions and organizations, it is possible that a particular information system may involve multiple AOs. If so, agreements should be established among the AOs and documented in the SSP. In most cases, it will be advantageous to agree to a Lead AO to represent the interests of the other AOs. An AO can also delegate an Authorizing Official Designated Representative (AODR) to make mission risk determinations. However, the ultimate decision on the acceptability of such risk is the responsibility of the authorizing official. 3.3.6 Information System Owner (SO) The responsibility of the SO, as defined by NIST SP 800-37, is the overall procurement, development, integration, modification, or operation and maintenance of an information system. The SO is responsible for the development and maintenance of the SSP and ensures the system is deployed and operated according to the agreed-upon security requirements. The SO is also responsible for deciding who has access to the information system (and with what types of privileges or access rights) and ensures that system users and support personnel receive the requisite security training (e.g., instruction in RoB). The SO informs key agency officials of the need to conduct a security C&A of the information system, ensures that appropriate resources are available for the effort, and provides the necessary system-related documentation to the Certification Agent (CA). The SO receives the security assessment results from the CA. After taking appropriate steps to reduce or eliminate vulnerabilities, the SO assembles the SAP and submits the package to the AO or the AODR for adjudication. 3.3.7 Information Owner (IO) The responsibilities of the IO are generally defined in NIST SP 800-37. The IO has statutory or operational authority for specified information and responsibility for establishing the controls for its generation, collection, processing, dissemination, and disposal. The IO is responsible for establishing the rules for appropriate use and protection of the subject information (e.g., RoB) and retains that responsibility even when the information is shared with other organizations. The owner of the information stored within, processed by, or transmitted by an information system may or may not be the same as the SO. Also, a single information system may utilize information from multiple IOs. The IOs should provide input to SOs regarding the security requirements and security controls for the information systems where the information resides. 3.3.8 Information System Security Officer (ISSO) The responsibility of the ISSO, as defined by NIST SP 800-37, is to ensure the appropriate operational security posture is maintained for an information system or program. The ISSO also serves as the principal advisor to the ITSO/SAISO, and SO on all security matters for the information system. In close coordination with the SO, the ISSO often plays an active role in developing and updating the SSP, as well as in managing and controlling changes to the system and assessing the security impact of those changes.

10 For Official Use Only

Census Bureau IT Security Policies

April 2010

3.3.9 Certification Agent (CA) The CA, as defined by NIST SP 800-37, is an individual, group, or organization responsible for conducting a security certification, or comprehensive assessment of the management, operational, and technical security controls in an information system to determine the extent to which the controls are implemented correctly, operating as intended, and producing the desired outcome with respect to meeting the security requirements for the system. The CA also provides recommended corrective actions to reduce or eliminate vulnerabilities in the information system. Prior to initiating the security assessment activities that are a part of the certification process, the CA provides an independent assessment of the SSP to ensure the plan provides a set of security controls for the information system that is adequate to meet all applicable security requirements. 3.3.10 Information Security Manager The Information Security Manager serves as the principal security risk advisor, provides oversight functions, and coordinates and disseminates information security matters on behalf of a directorate. This role is often supported by appropriate coordinating roles (e.g., internet coordinators, Division Security Coordinators, property custodians, data custodians, ISSOs, which may be direct reports to the Information Security Manager. The Information Security Manager ensures that: (i) security risk-related considerations for individual information systems are viewed from a directorate-wide perspective with regard to the overall strategic goals and objectives of the directorate in carrying out its missions and business functions; and (ii) managing risk from individual information systems is consistent across the directorate, reflects organizational risk tolerance, and is considered along with other organizational risks in order to ensure mission or business success. The Information Security Manager also acts as the principal liaison with the SAISO to ensure that the directorate's security posture is compliant with applicable Federal laws as well as Departmental and Bureau policies. He/She will act as the principal person responsible for ensuring that information relating to information security is communicated throughout the directorate. 3.3.11 Division Security Coordinator (DSC) The Division Security Coordinator is responsible for coordinating division activities in support of meeting information security requirements and best practices. The Division Security Coordinator is a role that is focused on the coordination of security activities on behalf of a division, where as the Information System Security Officer (ISSO) is a role which is focused on an information system. The Division Security Coordinator assists the Information System Security Officer(s), as necessary, in support of Certification and Accreditation of Information Systems within the division (e.g., participate in risk assessments, development of Interagency Security Agreements, Memorandums of Understandings, Contingency Plans, Business Impact Assessments, etc.).

3.4

The Department may define additional roles and delegate responsibilities to the individuals in this section. 3.4.1 Contracting Officer (CO) The CO is responsible for managing contracts/acquisitions. This includes overseeing their implementation, and works in partnership with the SAISO to ensure that contracting policies

adequately address the information and technology security requirements and collaborating with the Contracting Officer's Technical Representatives (COTRs) to monitor contract performance for compliance with DOC, OU, and application specific information security policies. Specifically, the COTRs shall: Ensure foreign nationals will not be granted access to or perform duties on IT systems without appropriate background checks, as defined by the DOC Security Manual, Chapter 16 and DAO 207-12. Notify SOs of new users and notify them to revoke access privileges in a timely manner when a user under his/her supervision or oversight no longer requires access privileges or he/she fails to comply with this policy. Authorize remote access privileges for personnel and review remote access user security agreements on an annual basis to verify the continuing need for access, the appropriate level of privileges, and the accuracy of information contained in the agreement (e.g., systems authorized for access and type and version of anti-virus software and personal firewall). 3.4.3 Supervisor The responsibilities of a supervisor encompass the management of subordinate users, which includes assessing, authorizing and managing the need for access to Census Bureau information and/or technological resources, and taking immediate action if misuse is suspected or confirmed as defined under user responsibilities, OU and/or application specific agreements. Specifically, supervisors shall: Ensure foreign nationals will not be granted access to or perform duties on IT systems without appropriate background checks, as defined by the DOC Security Manual, Chapter 16. Notify SOs of new users and notify them to revoke access privileges in a timely manner when a user under his/her supervision or oversight no longer requires access privileges or he/she fails to comply with this policy. Authorize remote access privileges for personnel and review remote access user security agreements on an annual basis to verify the continuing need for access, the appropriate level of privileges, and the accuracy of information contained in the agreement (e.g.,

systems authorized for access and type and version of anti-virus software and personal firewall). 3.4.4 Account, Application, Database, Network and System Administrators Account, Application, Database, Network and System Administrators, under the Supervisor/SO direction and specifications, are responsible for implementing IT security controls, OU-specific and application-specific policies, which minimally includes involvement of Developers and Programmers for routine testing. 3.4.5 Developers and Programmers Developers and Programmers must implement IT security controls in systems and system components (including software) as specified by the Supervisor/SO to ensure compliance with IT security controls, OU-specific, and application-specific policies. This minimally includes involvement with User Representatives and in system certification activities, such as documentation of new system components and vulnerability testing, as well as adhering to change management guidelines. 3.4.6 Key Contingency Roles Key contingency roles, such as those defined in COOP, Disaster Recovery, and IT Contingency Plans have responsibilities to ensure that the respective plan is maintained, tested, integrated with other plans, is adequate in scope, and relevant. 3.4.7 IT Security Incident Response Personnel The IT Security Incident Response Personnel responsibilities include analyzing and reducing cyber threats and vulnerabilities, disseminating cyber threat warning information, coordinating incident response activities, interacting with the DOC Federation of Computer Incident Response Teams (FedCIRTs) and others to disseminate reasoned and actionable cyber security information as necessary. Responsibilities include assuring that coordination with the US-CERT and appropriate authorities occurs as necessary. 3.4.8 Users/Stewards Users are defined as any individual having non-public access to Census Bureau information and/or technological resources. This scope includes those who may only have physical access within Census Bureau facilities, or those who may only have access to shared technological resources. All users must read, understand, and acknowledge understanding of Census Bureau and applicable application-specific policies. At a minimum, users shall: Complete IT Security refresher training annually; Understand Census Bureau property (or assets) for which user is responsible (i.e., printer, desktop, etc.); Know the type of data which is handled, and understand measures to protect the data type; Understand and be proactive in management of Federal electronic records, which extends to assurance of appropriate back-ups of user data;

13 For Official Use Only

Census Bureau IT Security Policies

April 2010

Cooperate with designated personnel during the investigation of incidents, compliance reviews, audits and/or surveys regarding the security posture of the Census Bureau; Report suspected or confirmed security incidents (e.g., loss of Personally Identifiable Information (PII), virus or malicious code attacks, etc.) as procedurally defined by the Census Bureau; Obey copyrights and do not download, install, or access Peer-to-Peer (P2P) file sharing software; Understand only approved individuals are allowed to download and install approved applications onto BOC IT resources; and Understand and/or discuss the consequences of actions of misuse; and, Understand that all use and content of IT systems, including computers, may be monitored, and reviewed for security purposes.

3.5

DOC IT GROUPS

Depending on the current DOC security posture, environment, or architecture, other forums and/or groups are established to address or review a specific issue, or subject area. Minimally, the following forums have been established to ensure continuous collaboration at multiple levels. 3.5.1 CIO Council As defined in DOO 15-23, the CIO Council promotes effective IT management practices throughout the Department and shares information of a crosscutting nature and is chaired by the DOC CIO. 3.5.2 Commerce IT Review Board (CITRB) As defined in DOO 15-23, the CITRB is chaired by the DOC CIO, reviews and evaluates proposed IT initiatives and requests for acquisitions, reviews and evaluates ongoing IT projects, and guides a capital asset management process. 3.5.3 Enterprise Architecture (EA) Advisory Group The EA Advisory Group serves as a Department-wide forum for definition of a blueprint that explains how the results of strategic planning, performance planning, budgeting, capital planning and investment control, security and privacy, acquisition, and other related IT and general management processes work together to meet the enterprise's mission and objectives. The EA defines the future state of DOC's IT based on business and technology drivers as well as the transition plan for moving from the current state to the future. 3.5.4 IT Security Coordinating Committee (ITSCC) The ITSCC serves as a Department-wide forum for sharing information addressing issues and making recommendations related to IT security responsibilities and activities that affect the DOC as a whole. The ITSCC is subordinate to, reports to the CIO Council, and is sponsored by the DOC CIO. The DOC CISO facilitates the ITSCC. 3.5.5 Webmaster Advisory Group (WAG) The WAG serves as a Department-wide forum for the DOC Internet and Intranet presence; website and web server security issues; and Departmental Internet policy issues in support of EGovernment. The WAG is an advisory body to the DOC CIO and the CIO Council.
14 For Official Use Only

Census Bureau IT Security Policies

April 2010

3.5.6 Electronic and IT (EIT) Accessibility Coordinator and Commerce Information Quality Task Force The EIT Accessibility Coordinator disseminates information on EIT accessibility matters to the OUs and facilitates cooperation among them on accessibility issues. The Information Quality Act mandates the issuance of information quality guidelines. This legislation affords Commerce the opportunity to highlight its commitment to information quality by posting its information quality and peer review guidelines to demonstrate our thorough and professional approach to information release. The Commerce Information Quality Task Force is comprised of the Office of the Secretary and OU staff that coordinates the implementation of the Act and communicates implementation status with the OMB.

3.6

CENSUS BUREAU IT GROUPS

3.6.1 Census Bureau IT Governing Board (ITGB) The Census Bureau ITGB reviews and evaluates proposed IT initiatives and requests for acquisitions, and also reviews and evaluates ongoing IT projects, and guides a capital asset management process, and is chaired by the Census Bureau CIO. 3.6.2 Data Stewardship Executive Policy Committee The DSEP serves as the Census Bureau Executive Staff focal point for decision-making and communication on policy issues related to privacy, security, confidentiality, and administrative records. The DSEP acts on behalf of the full Executive Staff in setting new policy and making decisions on policy-related matters that touches on these issues throughout the Census Bureau. The mission of DSEP is to assure that the Census Bureau can effectively collect and use data about the nation's people and economy, while fully meeting the Census Bureau's legal and ethical obligations to respondents to respect privacy and protect confidentiality. This includes fully meeting the legal, ethical and reporting obligations to levied by the Census Bureau Act (Title 13), the Privacy Act, and other applicable statutes, including those of governmental and other suppliers of data to the Census Bureau. The DSEP is responsible for effectively safeguarding and facilitating legitimate access to information required to fulfill the agency's mission, including mission-oriented and administrative information. 3.6.3 Census Bureau IT Security Office Under the direction of the Census Bureau ITSO/SAISO, the Census Bureau IT Security Office staff is responsible for the technical implementation and management of the Census Bureau IT Security Program. Additionally, the ITSO is supplemented with contractors who perform C&A services to System Owners/Program Areas.

3.7

DOC OFFICES

Given the reliance on and use of information technology, all DOC offices must coordinate, particularly with the OCIO. This includes, but is not limited to, the following offices: CFO/Assistant Secretary for Administration, Office of General Counsel (OGC), Office of the Inspector General (OIG), Office of Legislative and Intergovernmental Affairs (OLIA), Office of Policy and Strategic Planning (OPSP), Office of Public Affairs (OPA).

3.7.1 Office of the Chief Information Officer (OCIO) As defined in DOO 15-23, the OCIO is responsible for implementing the Clinger-Cohen Act of 1996, leads the management of information resources throughout the Department, ensuring that the Department's programs make full and appropriate use of IT. 3.7.2 Office of IT Security, Infrastructure and Technology (OITSIT) As defined in DOO 15-23, the OITSIT shall manage and implement the Department-wide IT Security Program and the Department-wide CIP, including: development and promulgation of policy and procedures; monitoring compliance of OUs; overseeing OU IT Security Programs; and management of the DOC FedCIRTs. 3.7.3 Office of Security (OSY) The OSY is responsible for the physical and environmental security controls that protect the DOC's information system assets. Facility security and access are maintained by this office. These controls include ensuring the COOP development and continuity of government programs, security clearance management, and physical access control mechanisms. The OSY is responsible for: Physical security of facilities and equipment external to computers or telecommunication lines; Protection of national security information; Personnel security, including performance of background checks and security clearance investigations of personnel; Coordinating with the DOC CIPM on the physical security aspect of critical infrastructure protection; Emergency planning; and, Conducting investigations to identify and/or assess threats to the Department's mission, operations, or activities and protect Department personnel, facilities, property, or assets including IT-related incidents with a counterintelligence, criminal intelligence or counterterrorism nexus. Further information is available in Manual of Security Policies and Procedures (Chapters 1 and 2), and the appropriate Departmental directives (i.e., the DAO 207 series, Security and Loyalty). 3.7.4 Office of Acquisition Management and Financial Assistance (OAM) The OAM ensures that appropriate information security clauses, and other terms and conditions, are inserted into procurement documents and contracts in accordance with the DOC security policies, CAR and FAR. The OAM, in conjunction with the OGC and OITSIT, develops and uses security clauses, as appropriate, based on current policies, regulations, and guidance for DOC information systems and services. The OAM ensures the integrity of procurements for the Department as a whole. In addition, the Department's Procurement Executive delegates procurement warrant authority to DOC Heads of Contract Offices (HCOs). By ensuring that contract vehicles address appropriate security measures, the HCO manages subordinate Bureau Procurement Offices (BPOs), which play a critical role in the beginning and throughout the lifecycle management process for IT service
16 For Official Use Only

Census Bureau IT Security Policies

April 2010

acquisitions. The HCOs and BPOs also play a critical role during the Development/Acquisition stage of system lifecycle management. The OUs consult with its BPO during the development of IT system security acquisitions. Development of acquisition requirements is integral to the lifecycle process. The BPO obtains the OU's requirements in the areas of technical features (e.g., access controls); personnel security (e.g., background checks for system developers); and operational practices (e.g., awareness and training) in the form of a statement of work prepared by the OU. After the OU has determined security features and requirements, and provided the Special Projects Office (SPO) with its Statement of Work, the SPO CO works with the Acquisition Team to ensure the solicitation, and later contract award, include the security requirements. The OU ITSOs/SAIAOs, SOs, COs, COTRs, and others involved in aspects of system security shall follow a methodology consistent with NIST SP 800-64, Security Considerations in the Information System Development Life Cycle. This methodology ensures that IT security is addressed in the acquisition process. The DOC requires that acquisition professionals (e.g., COs and Contract Specialists) provide a valuable service by ensuring that their customers work with OUs, including ITSOs, to address security in their IT contract requirements in all stages of an acquisition (i.e., from the earliest budgeting and acquisition planning stages through requirements development, solicitation, source evaluation and selection, contract award and administration). The CAM, Section 1337.70, Security Processing Requirements for On-Site Security Requirements requires the customer to work with their respective security office before a solicitation is released to designate contract risk levels (for all on-site contracts, not just IT) and then after award to arrange for background investigations on contractor employees in accordance with DOC Manual of Security Policies and Procedures, Chapter 11. The OU shall provide the BPO with the appropriate risk determination for the contract, and the BPO includes the corresponding appropriate language in the contract. 3.7.5 Office of Human Resources Management (OHRM) The OHRM maintains the memorandum of agreement between the National Finance Center (NFC) and DOC. The MOU is for the NFC to provide services for maintaining the NFC database with DOC employee information. This database may be utilized for maintaining a credentials management system and authorization of individual employee physical access controls at the OU. The NFC database manages personnel information used to perform background checks and other investigative information. In addition, the NFC database may be used to document the status of personnel access to information resources (e.g., employment status). The NFC database is a resource used in conjunction with OSY resources to maintain the status of physical access credentials such as building passes and badges for employees and contractors. This database consists of Privacy Act (PA) information which must be maintained consistent with PA requirements and can only be disclosed pursuant to disclosure provisions of the PA.

17 For Official Use Only

Census Bureau IT Security Policies

April 2010

The SHRO manages the human resources records for all OU personnel. The responsibilities of SHRO for the maintenance of security of IT resources include: Providing timely and accurate information concerning personnel hiring, transfer, and termination to the OU ITSO/SAISO; Assisting in the administration of IT Security Awareness training for new employees in accordance with the DOC Manual of Security Policies and Procedures, Chapter 3; Maintaining records concerning personnel security violations if resulting in disciplinary action; Maintaining position descriptions for all positions within serviced area; Developing and providing guidance on procedures for disciplinary and/or adverse action due to IT security violations; and, Maintaining personnel records containing the status of background checks, employment renewals and investigations of all personnel in accordance with the DOC Manual of Security Policies and Procedures, Chapter 11. 3.7.6 Office of Inspector General (OIG) The OIG provides independent oversight through audit and evaluation of the Department's IT Security Program, in accordance with the Inspector General Act of 1978 (Public Law 95-452). In this capacity, the OIG conducts audits of financial system controls, and evaluates the Department's compliance with FISMA requirements. The OIG also assists in the investigation of computer incidents that require coordination with external law enforcement agencies. Policies relating to these areas can be found in appropriate Departmental directives, e.g., Inspector General Investigations, DAO 207-10. Each OU CIO or OU ITSO/SAISO should maintain cooperative relationships with the OIG, including specific agreements and procedures covering incident response and forensics investigations if applicable. Incidents involving suspected fraud, waste, or abuse of government resources should be reported to the OIG Fraud Hotline for investigation. 3.7.7 Office of General Counsel (OGC) The OGC develops security clauses, as appropriate, based on current policies, regulations, and guidance for DOC information systems and services in conjunction with OITSIT and OAMFA. The OGC helps by reviewing DOC IT security policies to ensure the policies are aligned with current legal requirements. The OGC also reviews the legality of IT security contract clauses used by OAMFA in DOC contracts.

4.0 IT SECURITY POLICY CONTROLS
The following sections describe the security controls required for low, moderate, and high-baseline information systems, as defined by NIST 800-53, Revision 3 and the Census Bureau ITSO. The requirements documented herein represent the minimum security requirements for each security baseline; additionally, System Owners may, at their discretion, elect to include additional controls documented below, including non-selected security controls (those not required for any systems). If non-selected controls are included in an information system baseline, it is the responsibility of the System Owner to define any control assignments and selections in the information system security plan.

4.1

ACCESS CONTROL

Class: Technical Logical access controls are the system-based mechanisms used to designate who or what is to have access to a specific system resource and the type of transactions and functions that are permitted. They include controls that: Restrict users to authorized transactions and functions, and Limit network access and public access to the system.
Control Number Control Name/Requirement Security Baselines Low Moderate High

Access Control Policy and Procedures The Census Bureau IT Security Program Policies document represents the formal documented Census Bureau information security policies and addresses purpose, scope, roles, responsibilities, and compliance as they pertain to information security. Enterprise-level procedural documentation has been developed by ITSO to provide general guidelines for control implementation. The policy and procedures must be reviewed, updated and disseminated at least every other year.

AC-1

X

20 For Official Use Only

Census Bureau IT Security Policies

April 2010
Security Baselines Low Moderate High

Control Number

Control Name/Requirement

Account Management Program Offices/System Owners must manage information system accounts by: a) Identifying account types (i.e., individual, group, system, application, guest/anonymous, and temporary); b) Establishing conditions for group membership; c) Identifying authorized users of the information system and specifying access privileges; d) Requiring appropriate approvals for requests to establish accounts; e) Establishing, activating, modifying, disabling, and removing accounts; f) Specifically authorizing and monitoring the use of guest/anonymous and temporary accounts; g) Notifying account managers when temporary accounts are no longer required and when information system users are terminated, transferred, or information system usage or needto-know/need-to-share changes; h) Deactivating: (i) temporary accounts that are no longer required and (ii) accounts of terminated or transferred users; i) Granting access to the system based on: (i) a valid access authorization; (ii) intended system usage; and (iii) other attributes as required by the organization or associated missions/business functions; and j) Reviewing accounts at least semi-annually. Automated mechanisms must be employed to support the management of information system accounts. Information systems must automatically terminate temporary and emergency accounts after 30 days. Information systems must automatically disable inactive accounts after 30 days. Automated mechanisms must be employed to ensure that account creation, modification, disabling, and termination actions are audited and, as required, appropriate individuals must be notified. Currently, the NIST Special Publication 800-53 Rev. 3 does not mandate implementation of this control for low, moderate, or high baseline systems. Therefore, the Census Bureau will not assess any systems according to this control. Program Offices/System Owners may elect to: a) Require that users log out when [Assignment: organization defined time-period of expected inactivity and/or description of when to log out]; b) Determine normal time-of-day and duration usage for information system accounts; c) Require that information system accounts are monitored for atypical usage; and d) Require that atypical usage is reported to designated Census Bureau officials.

Separation of Duties Program Offices/System Owners must ensure that information systems: a) Separate duties of individuals as necessary, to prevent malevolent activity without collusion; b) Document separation of duties; and c) Implement separation of duties through assigned information system access authorizations. Appropriate divisions of responsibility must be established to eliminate conflicts of interest in the responsibility and duties of individuals. Examples of separation of duties include: (i) mission functions and distinct information systems support functions are divided among different individuals/ roles; (ii) different individuals perform information system support functions; (iii) security personnel who administer access control functions do not administer audit functions; and (iv) different administrator accounts for different roles.

Control Number

Control Name/Requirement

DOC Criteria The following three (3) categories of "duty" must be kept separate or compensating controls in place to monitor activity closely. IT Administration or operation (assuring systems function, to serve the system users); AC-5.1 IT Security (assuring adequacy of system controls for availability, integrity, and confidentiality); and IT Management (allocating adequate resources for implementation of effective IT Security Programs and system controls. DOC Criteria Due to staffing constraints, OUs may authorize the use of dual roles (e.g., a System Administrator may serve as a back-up for an ISSO who AC-5.2 is on leave). However, while serving in a dual role, compensating management controls must be implemented to ensure changes to the security posture are properly authorized. Least Privilege Program Offices/System Owners must ensure that information systems employ the concept of least privilege, allowing only authorized accesses for users (and processes acting on behalf of users) which are necessary to accomplish assigned tasks in accordance with Census Bureau missions and business functions. Access to establish system accounts, configure access authorizations (i.e. permissions, privileges), set events to be audited, and set intrusion detection parameters must be explicitly authorized. Users of information system accounts, or roles, with access to establish system accounts, configure access authorizations (i.e. permissions, privileges), set events to be audited, and set intrusion detection parameters must use non-privileged accounts, or roles, when accessing other system functions, and if feasible, use of privileged accounts must be audited for such functions. Currently, the NIST Special Publication 800-53 Rev. 3 does not mandate implementation of this control for low, moderate, or high baseline systems. Therefore, the Census Bureau will not assess any systems according to this control. Program Offices/System Owners may elect to require that network access to [Assignment: organization-defined privileged commands] is authorized only for compelling operational needs and that the rationale for such access is documented in the security plan for the information system. Currently, the NIST Special Publication 800-53 Rev. 3 does not mandate implementation of this control for low, moderate, or high baseline systems. Therefore, the Census Bureau will not assess any systems according to this control. Program Offices/System Owners may elect to require that information systems provide separate processing domains to enable finer-grained allocation of user privileges.

Unsuccessful Login Attempts Program Offices/System Owners must ensure that information systems: a) Enforce a limit of five (5) consecutive invalid login attempts by a user during a 15 minute time period; and b) Automatically lock the account for a minimum of 15 minutes, when the maximum number of unsuccessful attempts is exceeded. This control applies regardless of whether the login occurs via a local or network connection. Currently, the NIST Special Publication 800-53 Rev. 3 does not mandate implementation of this control for low, moderate, or high baseline systems. Therefore, the Census Bureau will not assess any systems according to this control. Program Offices/System Owners may elect to require that information systems automatically lock the account/node until released by an administrator when the maximum number of unsuccessful attempts is exceeded. Currently, the NIST Special Publication 800-53 Rev. 3 does not mandate implementation of this control for low, moderate, or high baseline systems. Therefore, the Census Bureau will not assess any systems according to this control. Program Offices/System Owners may elect to require that information systems provide additional protection for mobile devices accessed via login by purging information from the devices after [Assignment: organization-defined number] consecutive, unsuccessful login attempts to the device. DOC Criteria Locked accounts with privileged access (i.e., root or administrator access) will remain locked until unlocked by the respective Help Desk, Security Administrator, or other authorized account management personnel whereby reasonable and verifiable identification is employed.

Control Name/Requirement

System Use Notification Program Offices/System Owners must ensure that information systems: a) Display an approved system use notification message or banner before granting access to the system that states that: (i) the user is accessing a U.S. government information system; (ii) system usage may be monitored, recorded, and subject to audit; (iii) unauthorized system use is prohibited and subject to criminal and civil penalties; and (iv) use of the system indicates consent to monitoring and recording; b) Retain the notification message or banner on the screen until the user takes explicit actions to log on to or further access the information system; and c) For publicly assessable systems: (i) display the system use information when appropriate, before granting further access; (ii) display references, if any, to monitoring, recording, or auditing that are consistent with privacy accommodations for such systems that generally prohibit those activities; and (iii) include a description of the authorized uses of the system in the notice given to the public users of the information system. AC-8 The following is the official Census Bureau warning banner: **WARNING**WARNING**WARNING**WARNING**WARNING** This is a Census Bureau computer system. Census Bureau computer systems are provided for the processing of official U.S. Government information only. All data contained within Census Bureau computer systems is owned by the Census Bureau and may be monitored intercepted recorded read copied or captured in any manner and disclosed in any manner by authorized personnel. THERE IS NO RIGHT OF PRIVACY IN THIS SYSTEM. System personnel may disclose any potential evidence of crime found on Census Bureau computer systems to appropriate authorities. USE OF THIS SYSTEM BY ANY USER AUTHORIZED OR UNAUTHORIZED CONSTITUTES CONSENT TO THIS MONITORING INTERCEPTION RECORDING READING COPYING CAPTURING and DISCLOSURE OF COMPUTER ACTIVITY. Use of this computer without authorization or for unauthorized purposes is a violation of federal law and punishable by fines or imprisonment (Public Law 99-474). **WARNING**WARNING**WARNING**WARNING**WARNING** Currently, the NIST Special Publication 800-53 Rev. 3 does not mandate implementation of this control for low, moderate, or high baseline systems. Therefore, the Census Bureau will not assess any systems according to this control. Program Offices/System Owners may elect to require that information systems notify users, upon successful logon/access, of the date and time of the last logon/access. X X X

AC-9.2

Currently, the NIST Special Publication 800-53 Rev. 3 does not mandate implementation of this control for low, moderate, or high baseline systems. Therefore, the Census Bureau will not assess any systems according to this control. AC-9.3 Program Offices/System Owners may elect to require that information systems notify users of [Assignment: organization-defined set of security-related changes to the user's account] during [Assignment: organization-defined time period]. Concurrent Session Control Program Offices/System Owners must ensure that information systems limit the number of concurrent sessions for each system account to a maximum of 5 sessions. Program Offices/System Owners must define in their security plans the number of concurrent sessions a user is allowed. Concurrent sessions must be kept to as low as possible based on risk. Program Offices/System Owners must ensure that information systems: a) Prevent further access to the system by initiating a session lock after 15 minutes of inactivity or upon receiving a request from a user; b) Retain the session lock until the user reestablishes access using established identification and authentication procedures. "Inactivity" is defined as only those actions which would require interaction of a user (i.e., system and application calls are not included) Currently, the NIST Special Publication 800-53 Rev. 3 does not mandate implementation of this control for low, moderate, or high baseline systems. Therefore, the Census Bureau will not assess any systems according to this control. Program Offices/System Owners may elect to require that information systems implement a session lock mechanism that, when activated on a device with a display screen, places a publicly viewable pattern onto the associated display, hiding what was previously visible on the screen.

AC-16.5

Program Offices/System Owners may elect to require that information systems display security attributes in human-readable form on each object output from the system to system output devices to identify [Assignment: organization-identified set of special dissemination, handling, or distribution instructions] using [Assignment: organization-defined identified human readable, standard naming conventions]. Program Offices/System Owners must ensure that: a) Allowed methods of remote access (i.e., access external to the Census Bureau) to information systems are documented; b) Usage restrictions and implementation guidance for each allowed remote access method are established; c) Unauthorized remote access to information systems is monitored; d) Remote access to information systems is authorized prior to connection; and e) Requirements for remote connections to information systems are enforced. Remote Access to the Census Bureau systems is only permitted for emergency remote administration of servers and applications (for contingency purposes). The Census Bureau does not allow remote access for teleworking. Automated mechanisms must be employed to facilitate the monitoring and control of remote access methods. Encryption must be used to protect the confidentiality and integrity of remote access sessions. All remote access must be controlled through a limited number of managed access points. Execution of privileged commands and access to security-relevant information via remote access must be authorized only for compelling operational needs and the rationale for such access must be documented in the security plans of information systems. Program Offices/System Owners must monitor for unauthorized remote connections to the information system at least monthly and take appropriate actions if an unauthorized connection is discovered. Currently, the NIST Special Publication 800-53 Rev. 3 does not mandate implementation of this control for low, moderate, or high baseline systems. Therefore, the Census Bureau will not assess any systems according to this control. Program Offices/System Owners may elect to require that users protect information about remote access mechanisms from unauthorized use and disclosure.

Wireless Access Restrictions Program Offices/System Owners must: a) Establish usage restrictions and implementation guidance for wireless access; b) Monitor for unauthorized wireless access to information systems; c) Authorize wireless system access prior to connection; and d) Enforce requirements for wireless connections to information systems. Authentication and encryption must be used to protect wireless access to information systems.

Control Number

Control Name/Requirement

Access Control for Portable and Mobile Systems Program Offices/System Owners must ensure that: a) Usage restrictions and implementation guidance for Census Bureau-controlled mobile devices are established; b) Connection of mobile devices meeting organizational usage restrictions and implementation guidance to Census Bureau information systems are authorized; c) Census Bureau information systems are monitored for unauthorized connections of mobile devices; d) Requirements for the connection of mobile devices to Census Bureau information systems are enforced; e) Information system functionality that provides the capability for automatic execution of code on mobile devices with user direction is disabled; f) Specially configured mobile devices are issued to individuals traveling to locations that the Census Bureau deems to be of significant risk; and g) Mobile devices returning from locations that the Census Bureau deems to be of significant risk are examined for signs of physical tampering and/or purging/reimaging of the hard disk drive. System Owners, in coordination with the ITSO, must authorize the use of portable and mobile devices based on system sensitivity and risk level. Only FIPS 140-2 compliant flash drives supplied by the IT Directorate are authorized for storing Census Bureau information. Personally Identifiable Information (PII) must not be stored on laptops or external or removable devices that are not encrypted with FIPS 140-2 compliant full disk encryption. Portable devices should be scanned for malware prior to use on Census Bureau networks. Use of writable, removable media must be restricted in Census Bureau information systems. Use of personally owned, removable media must be prohibited in Census Bureau information systems. Use of removable media in Census Bureau information systems must be prohibited when the media has no identifiable owner.

4.2

IT SECURITY AWARENESS AND TRAINING

Class: Operational A strong IT security program cannot be put in place without significant attention given to training agency IT users on security policy, procedures, and techniques, as well as the various management, operational, and technical controls necessary and available to secure IT resources. In addition, those in the agency who manage the IT infrastructure need to have the necessary skills to carry out their assigned duties effectively. Failure to give attention to the area of security training puts an enterprise at great risk because security of agency resources is as much a human issue as it is a technology issue.1
Control Number Security Baselines Control Name/Requirement Low Moderate High

Security Awareness and Training Policy and Procedures The Census Bureau IT Security Program Policies document represents the formal documented Census Bureau information security policies, and addresses purpose, scope, roles, responsibilities, and compliance as they pertain to information security. Enterprise-level procedural documentation has been developed by ITSO to provide general guidelines for control implementation. The policy and procedures must be reviewed, updated and disseminated at least every other year. Program Offices/System Owners must ensure all users (including managers and senior executive staff) are provided and complete basic information system security awareness training/materials within 30 days of appointment and before authorizing access to the system. Awareness training must be provided and completed annually thereafter.

4.3

AUDIT AND ACCOUNTABILITY

Class: Technical Audit trails maintain a record of system activity by system or application processes and by user activity and processes. In conjunction with appropriate tools and procedures, audit trails can provide individual accountability, a means to reconstruct events, detect intrusions, and identify problems. System audit trails, or event logs, provide a record of events in support of activities to monitor and enforce the IT system security policy. The NIST SP 800-12, An Introduction to Computer Security: The NIST Handbook, Chapter 18, describes an event as any action that happens on a computer system, such as logging into a system, executing a program, and opening a file. All audit logs are subject to recording and routine review by the Census Bureau ITSO and auditors for inappropriate or illegal activity. System owners must ensure the protection of system event logs with filelevel permissions, separation of duties, and all other safeguards commensurate with the highest level of sensitivity of the information residing on the system for which the logs record data.
Control Number Security Baselines Control Name/Requirement Low Moderate High

Audit and Accountability Policy and Procedures The Census Bureau IT Security Program Policies document represents the formal documented Census Bureau information security policies and addresses purpose, scope, roles, responsibilities, and compliance as they pertain to information security. Enterprise-level procedural documentation has been developed by ITSO to provide general guidelines for control implementation. The policy and procedures must be reviewed, updated and disseminated at least every other year. Program Offices/System Owners must ensure that: a) Based on a risk assessment and mission/business needs, information systems are capable of auditing the following events: Startup and shutdown Loading and unloading of services (only applicable to operating systems) Installation and removal of software (only applicable to operating systems) System alerts and error messages User logon and logoff System administration activities Modification of privileges and access controls b) Security audit function is coordinated with other Census Bureau entities requiring audit-related information to enhance mutual support and to help guide the selection of auditable events; c) A rationale for why the list of auditable events are deemed adequate to support after-the-fact investigations of security incidents is documented; and

Response to Audit Processing Failure Program Offices/Systems Owners must ensure that, in the event of an audit processing failure, information systems: a) Alert designated Census Bureau officials in the event of an audit failure or audit storage capacity being reached; and b) Either overwrite the oldest audit records or cease information system processing, depending on system data availability and integrity requirements. It is recommended that a justification for selection be documented in the system security plan. Information systems must provide a warning when allocated audit record storage volume reaches 90% of maximum audit record storage capacity. Information systems must provide a real-time alert when the audit storage capacity reaches 90%. Currently, the NIST Special Publication 800-53 Rev. 3 does not mandate implementation of this control for low, moderate, or high baseline systems. Therefore, the Census Bureau will not assess any systems according to this control. Program Offices/System Owners may elect to require that information systems provide the capability to: a) Capture/record and log all content related to a user session; and b) Remotely view/hear all content related to an established user session in real time. Currently, the NIST Special Publication 800-53 Rev. 3 does not mandate implementation of this control for low, moderate, or high baseline systems. Therefore, the Census Bureau will not assess any systems according to this control. Program Offices/System Owners may elect to require that information systems initiate session audits at system start-up.

4.4

CERTIFICATION, ACCREDITATION, AND SECURITY ASSESSMENTS

Class: Management C&A is the process of formal assessment, testing (certification), and acceptance (accreditation) of system security controls that protect IT systems and data stored in and processed by those systems. This process recognizes, evaluates, and assigns responsibility for the risk of operating an IT system, encompasses the system's life cycle, and ensures that the risk of operating a system is recognized, evaluated, and accepted. The C&A process implements the concept of "adequate security," or security commensurate with risk, including the magnitude of harm resulting from the unauthorized access, use, disclosure, disruption, modification, or destruction of information, which is defined in OMB Circular A-130. Although C&A are related, they are separate procedures and have different objectives. Certification is a short-term activity that is repeated after any significant system-related change is completed and is a prerequisite for accreditation. Accreditation is a long-term authorization, up to three years, that allows a system to operate based on the facts, plans, and schedules developed during certification. In the C&A process, there is an evaluation of the tests performed on security controls to determine (i) whether the residual risk to the system (risk not eliminated by implementation of counter measures) is acceptable; and (ii) whether the functioning controls provide adequate protection for the system to operate.
Control Number Security Baselines Control Name/Requirement Low Moderate High

Certification, Accreditation, and Security Assessments Policies and Procedures The Census Bureau IT Security Program Policies document represents the formal documented Census Bureau information security policies and addresses purpose, scope, roles, responsibilities, and compliance as they pertain to information security. Enterprise-level procedural documentation has been developed by ITSO to provide general guidelines for control implementation. The policy and procedures must be reviewed, updated and disseminated at least every other year. DOC Criteria The DOC requires OUs to follow the C&A process as detailed in NIST SP 800-37, Guide for the Security Certification and Accreditation of Federal Information Systems. o
