Information and System Connections Program Offices/System Owners must: a) Authorize connections from information systems to other information systems outside of their accreditation boundary through the use of Interconnection Security Agreements; b) Ensure that, for each connection, the interface characteristics, security requirements, and the nature of the information communicated are documented; and c) Ensure that information system connections are monitored on an ongoing basis, verifying enforcement of security requirements. DOC Criteria Conditions and subsequent requirements for interconnections are as follows: Interconnection with entities within DOC (OU to OU) requires establishment of an ISA, MOA or MOU. Interconnection with entities external to DOC requires establishment of a contract, ISA, MOA or MOU. For systems defined within the Census Bureau, interconnection agreements are required when there is a system interconnection from one information system to another information system outside of their defined accreditation boundary except for connections to infrastructure general support systems (e.g. CEN01, CEN16, CEN17) that provide inherited security controls. DOC Criteria The DOC requires the OUs to verify and document the security controls in the ISA, MOA, or MOU. DOC Criteria The DOC requires the OUs to restrict the use of personally owned information systems as recommended by the DOC CITR-002 Safeguarding Data on Foreign Travel.

DOC Criteria At a minimum, the DOC CISO and OU ITSO/SAISO must document in a POA&M all IT security control deficiencies warranting corrective action that were identified by: The Secretary of Commerce, and resulting in a material weakness in the Department's Annual Performance and Accountability Report; An external audit or evaluation (e.g., the GAO or the OIG); and, DOC compliance reviews, internal OU evaluations (e.g., SSPs documenting "planned" controls, self-assessments, periodic ST&Es, Contingency Plan testing, or through the system C&A process). DOC Criteria The DOC does not require that minor readily corrected weaknesses (e.g., on the spot corrections and those completed prior to the operation and maintenance phase of a system), or weakness considered by the AO to be acceptable residual risk, be tracked by the SO on a POA&M. However, the DOC does require that weaknesses of significant nature (e.g., those identified in the SSP as "planned" and those expressly identified by the AO in the accreditation decision letter) be tracked on a system-level POA&M.

4.5

CONFIGURATION MANAGEMENT

Class: Operational Configuration management describes the processes through which baseline configurations are developed and maintained for information systems and their constituent components, system configurations are compliant with Census Bureau security requirements, and all changes to system configurations are controlled and approved.The process of configuration management provides for a controlled environment in which changes to software and hardware are properly authorized, tested, and approved before implementation.
Control Number Security Baselines Control Name/Requirement Low Moderate High

Configuration Management Policy and Procedures The Census Bureau IT Security Program Policies document represents the formal documented Census Bureau information security policies, and addresses purpose, scope, roles, responsibilities, and compliance as they pertain to information security. Enterprise-level procedural documentation has been developed by ITSO to provide general guidelines for control implementation. The policy and procedures must be reviewed, updated and disseminated at least every other year. Program Offices/System Owners must ensure that current baseline configurations of information system components are developed, documented, and maintained under configuration control. Baseline configuration documentation must be reviewed and updated: a) At least annually; b) When required due to a significant system change; and c) As an integral part of information system component installations and upgrades. Automated mechanisms must be employed to maintain up-to-date, complete, accurate, and readily available baseline configurations for information system components. Older versions of baseline configurations must be retained as deemed necessary to support rollback. Program Offices/System Owners must ensure that: a) A list of software programs not authorized to execute on information systems is developed and maintained. Internally hosted systems must comply with the restrictions documented in the Software License Information Center (SLIC) system. Externally hosted systems must create a list of unauthorized software programs. b) An allow-all, deny-by-exception authorization policy is employed to identify software allowed to execute on information systems. Configuration Settings Program Offices/System Owners must ensure that: a) Mandatory configuration settings for the information technology products employed within information systems are established and documented using checklists compliant with the ITSO Secure Configuration Policy that reflect the most restrictive mode consistent with operational requirements; b) Configuration settings are implemented; c) Exceptions from the mandatory configuration settings for individual components within information systems are identified, documented, and approved based on explicit operational requirements; and d) Changes to configuration settings are monitored and controlled. Hardware is further defined as only those components that are "networked". DOC Criteria An inventory of software components depends on the system categorization, and minimally requires the following: 1. Low, Moderate, and High-impact systems require inventory of the operating system (to include version number). 2. Moderate and High-impact systems require inventory of the operating system and a list of core applications (to include version numbers). The OUs shall define "core applications." DOC Criteria Information System Component Inventories shall be updated at least annually as recommended by DOC CITR-003 Continuous Monitoring Plan. DOC Criteria OUs shall ensure that the component inventory is consistent with the accreditation boundary of the information system. o X

4.6

CONTINGENCY PLANNING

Class: Operational Federal agencies must have a plan in place to minimize the risk of disruptions to services they provide due to system unavailability. Contingency planning details the necessary procedures required to protect the continuing performance of business functions and services, including IT services, during an outage to successfully restore and operate systems and business functions during significant disruption.
Control Number Security Baselines Control Name/Requirement Low Moderate High

Contingency Planning Policy and Procedures The Census Bureau IT Security Program Policies document represents the formal documented Census Bureau information security policies, and addresses purpose, scope, roles, responsibilities, and compliance as they pertain to information security. Enterprise-level procedural documentation has been developed by ITSO to provide general guidelines for control implementation. The policy and procedures must be reviewed, updated and disseminated at least every other year. Program Offices/System Owners must ensure that: a) Contingency plans are developed for information systems that: Identify essential missions and business functions and associated contingency requirements; Provide recovery objectives, restoration priorities, and metrics; Address contingency roles, responsibilities, and assigned individuals with contact information; Address maintaining essential missions and business functions despite an information system disruption, compromise, or failure; Address eventual, full information system restoration without deterioration of the security measures originally planned and implemented; and Is reviewed and approved by designated Census Bureau officials; b) Copies of contingency plans are distributed to personnel identified in the system contingency plans; c) Contingency plan activities are coordinated with incident handling activities; d) Contingency plans for information systems are reviewed at least annually; e) Contingency plans are revised to address changes to the Census Bureau, information systems, or environment of operation and problems encountered during contingency plan implementation, execution, or testing; and f) Contingency plan changes are communicated to personnel identified in the system contingency plans.

Alternate Processing Sites CP-6.3 Program Offices/System Owners must ensure that; a) An alternate processing site is established, including necessary agreements to permit resumption of information system operations for essential missions and business functions within the time frame identified in the system contingency plan, when primary processing capabilities are unavailable; and b) Equipment and supplies required to resume operations are available at the alternate site or contracts are in place to support delivery to the site in time to support system resumption within the defined time period. Alternate processing sites must be fully configured and ready for use as the operational site supporting essential missions and business functions. Alternate processing sites must provide information security measures equivalent to that of the primary site, including physical, logical, and environmental security controls. If comparable security controls cannot be provided at the alternate processing site, these deviations must be documented in the system Contingency Plan along with applicable compensating controls.

4.7

IDENTIFICATION AND AUTHENTICATION

Class: Technical Identification and authentication is a technical measure that prevents unauthorized people (or unauthorized processes) from entering an IT system. Access control usually requires that the system be able to identify and differentiate users. All Census Bureau IT systems must have a means to enforce user accountability when using Census Bureau IT systems, so that system activity (both authorized and unauthorized) can be traced to specific users. To ensure user accountability, the Census Bureau requires that all IT systems implement a method of user identification and authentication. The user identification tells the system who the users are; the authentication mechanism provides an added level of assurance that the users really are who they say they are. Authentication consists of something a user knows (such as a password), something the user has (such as a token or smart card), or something the user is (such as a fingerprint). User identification and authentication also can enforce separation of duties.
Control Number Security Baselines Control Name/Requirement Low Moderate High

Identification and Authentication Policy and Procedures The Census Bureau IT Security Program Policies document represents the formal documented Census Bureau information security policies, and addresses purpose, scope, roles, responsibilities, and compliance as they pertain to information security. Enterprise-level procedural documentation has been developed by ITSO to provide general guidelines for control implementation. The policy and procedures must be reviewed, updated and disseminated at least every other year. Program Offices/System Owners must ensure information systems uniquely identify and authenticate users (or processes acting on behalf of users). User identification and authentication provides for accountability of user system activities and enforce separation of duties by limiting access. Multifactor authentication must be employed for network access to privileged accounts. Network access is defined as access to a system component (server, network device, application, or database) from a terminal that is physically separated from the system component. Multifactor authentication must be employed for network access to nonprivileged accounts. Network access is defined as access to a system component (server, application, etc) from a terminal that is physically separated from the component in question. Multifactor authentication must be employed for local access to privileged accounts. Local access is defined as access to a system component (server, application, etc) from a terminal that hosts the component in question. Multifactor authentication must be employed for local access to nonprivileged accounts. Local access is defined as access to a system component (server, application, etc) from a terminal that hosts the component in question.

Control Number

Authenticator Management Program Offices/System Owners must manage information system authenticators (e.g., tokens, PKI certificates, biometrics, passwords, and key cards) by: a) Verifying, as a part of initial authenticator distribution, the identity of the individual and/or device receiving the authenticator; b) Establishing initial authenticator content for authenticators defined by the Census Bureau; c) Ensuring that authenticators have sufficient strength of mechanism for their intended use; d) Establishing and implementing administrative procedures for initial authenticator distribution, for lost/compromised, or damaged authenticators, and revoking authenticators; e) Changing default authenticators upon information system installation; f) Establishing minimum and maximum lifetime restrictions and reuse conditions for authenticators (if appropriate); g) Changing/refreshing authenticators periodically; h) Protecting authenticator content from unauthorized disclosure and modification; and i) Requiring users to take, and have devices implement, specific measures to safeguard authenticators. Electronic authentication methods to provide services to citizens must comply with OMB Memorandum 04-04, E-Authentication Guidance for Federal Agencies, and associate implementation requirements in NIST SP 800-63, Electronic Authentication Guideline. For password-based authentication, information systems must: a) Enforce the following minimum password complexity requirements: At least twelve (12) non-blank characters; Characters from at least three (3) of the following four (4) categories: 1. English upper-case characters (A-Z); 2. English lower-case characters (a-z); 3. Base 10 digits (0-9); and 4. Non-Alphanumeric (ex.,!,$,#) b) Enforce at least one changed character when new passwords are created; c) Encrypt password in storage and in transmission; d) Enforce a password minimum lifetime restriction of one (1) day and a maximum lifetime restriction of 60 days; and e) Prohibit password reuse for a specific account for 24 generations or four (4) years.

Therefore, the Census Bureau will not assess any systems according to this control. Program Offices/System Owners may elect to take [Assignment: organization-defined measures] to manage the risk of compromise due to individuals having accounts on multiple information systems.

Cryptographic Module Authentication Program Offices/System Owners must ensure information systems employ mechanisms for authenticating to a cryptographic module (such as Safeboot, Secret Agent, Reflections, Hummingbird Exceed, etc) that meet the following requirements (and future amendments): NIST FIPS 140-1, Security Requirements for Cryptographic Modules NIST FIPS 140-2, Security Requirements for Cryptographic Modules The applicable federal standard for authenticating to a cryptographic module is FIPS 140-2 (as amended). 4.8

INCIDENT RESPONSE

Class: Operational An incident response capability is a mechanism through which Census Bureau system owners and the ITSO are kept informed of system vulnerability advisories from the US Computer Emergency Readiness Team (US-CERT), from software vendors, and other sources. The mechanism also ensures tracking and implementation of corrective actions (e.g., developing filter rules and patching) and coordinates with responsible incident response capabilities regarding the handling and reporting of incidents involving systems under the program area's responsibility. An incident response capability may consist of one or more persons (such as the ITSO or CIO), who ensure that vulnerability advisories are communicated to system owners.
Control Number Security Baselines Control Name/Requirement Low Moderate High

Incident Response Policy and Procedures The Census Bureau IT Security Program Policies document represents the formal documented Census Bureau information security policies and addresses purpose, scope, roles, responsibilities, and compliance as they pertain to information security. Enterprise-level procedural documentation has been developed by ITSO to provide general guidelines for control implementation. The policy and procedures must be reviewed, updated and disseminated at least every other year. Program Offices/System Owners must ensure that: a) Personnel are trained in their incident response roles and responsibilities with respect to information systems; b) Refresher training is provided at least annually. Simulated events must be incorporated into incident response training to facilitate effective personnel response in crisis situations.

Incident Response Plan Program Offices/System Owners must ensure that: a) An incident response plan is developed that: Provides the Census Bureau with a roadmap for implementing its incident response capability; Describes the structure and organization of the incident response capability; Provide a high-level approach for how the incident response capability fits into the overall Census Bureau organization; Meets unique Census Bureau requirements regarding mission, size, structure, and functions; Defines reportable incidents; Provides metrics for measuring the incident response capability within the Census Bureau; Defines the resources and management support necessary to effectively maintain and mature an incident response capability; and Is reviewed and approved by designated Census Bureau officials; b) Copies of the incident response plan are distributed to System Owners, ISSOs, Program Managers, and Division Chiefs; c) The incident response plan is reviewed annually; d) The incident response plan is revised to address changes to information systems or the Census Bureau or problems encountered during plan implementation, execution, or testing; and e) Incident response plan changes are communicated to System Owners, ISSOs, Program Managers, and Division Chiefs.

4.9

SYSTEM MAINTENANCE CONTROLS

Class: Operational System maintenance controls are used to monitor software installation and updates in order to ensure that systems function as expected, and that a historical record of changes is maintained. System maintenance controls are also used to limit the type of software installed on systems so as to prevent the installation and use of unauthorized software on Census Bureau systems.
Control Number Security Baselines Control Name/Requirement Low Moderate High

System Maintenance Policy and Procedures The Census Bureau IT Security Program Policies document represents the formal documented Census Bureau information security policies, and addresses purpose, scope, roles, responsibilities, and compliance as they pertain to information security. Enterprise-level procedural documentation has been developed by ITSO to provide general guidelines for control implementation. The policy and procedures must be reviewed, updated and disseminated at least every other year. Program Offices/System Owners must ensure that: a) Scheduling, performance, documentation, and review of records of maintenance and repairs on information system components is conducted in accordance with manufacturer or vendor specifications and/or Census Bureau requirements; b) All maintenance activities are controlled, whether performed on site or remotely and whether the equipment is serviced on site or removed to another location; c) A designated official explicitly approves the removal of information systems or information system components from Census Bureau facilities for off-site maintenance or repairs; d) Equipment is sanitized to remove all information from associated media prior to removal from Census Bureau facilities for off-site maintenance or repairs; and e) All potentially impacted security controls are checked to verify that the controls are still functioning properly following maintenance or repair actions. Program Offices/System Owners must ensure that maintenance records for information systems contain the following information: a) Date and time of maintenance; b) Name of the individual performing the maintenance; c) Name of escort, if necessary; d) A description of the maintenance performed; and e) A list of equipment removed or replaced (including identification numbers, if applicable). Automated mechanisms must be employed to schedule, conduct, and document maintenance and repairs required, producing up-to-date, accurate, complete, and available records of all maintenance and repair actions, needed, in process, and completed.

Maintenance Tools MA-3 Program Offices/System Owners must approve, control, and monitor the use of, and maintain on an ongoing basis, information system maintenance tools. All maintenance tools (e.g., diagnostic and test equipment) carried into Census Bureau facilities by maintenance personnel must be inspected for obvious improper modifications. All media containing diagnostic test programs (e.g., software or firmware used for system maintenance or diagnostics) must be checked for malicious code before the media is used in information systems. Program Offices/System Owners must prevent the unauthorized removal of maintenance equipment by one of the following: a) Verifying that there is no Census Bureau information contained on the equipment; b) Sanitizing or destroying the equipment; c) Retaining the equipment within the facility; d) Obtaining an exemption from a designated Census Bureau official explicitly authorizing removal of the equipment from the facility. All non-local maintenance and diagnostic sessions must be audited, and designated Census Bureau personnel must review the maintenance records of the sessions. 4.10 MEDIA PROTECTION
Class: Operational Media Protection controls ensure secure storage, handling, and destruction of IT information media.
Control Number Security Baselines Control Name/Requirement Low Moderate High

Media Protection Policy and Procedures The Census Bureau IT Security Program Policies document represents the formal documented Census Bureau information security policies and addresses purpose, scope, roles, responsibilities, and compliance as they pertain to information security. Enterprise-level procedural documentation has been developed by ITSO to provide general guidelines for control implementation. The policy and procedures must be reviewed, updated and disseminated at least every other year.

MP-1

X

X

X

DOC Criteria Electronic transmission of FOUO information is authorized by phone, fax, or e-mail when necessary for the conduct of official business. The FOUO information should be encrypted in transmission. However, a strict prohibition of such transmittal could seriously restrict the efficient MP-1.1 operation of an OU or office without the capability for encryption. All DOC personnel must understand that systems such as the Internet are untrusted, in that transmissions may be monitored, intercepted, and modified. Users should exercise caution before posting information or using the Internet for official government business. DOC Criteria Sensitive Compartmented Information (SCI) and facilities must be protected in accordance with Central Intelligence Agency directives, MP-1.2 Number 6 Series. DOC Security Manual, Section III, provides the protection requirements for the handling and marking of classified national security information. Media Access MP-2 Program Offices/System Owners must ensure that access to digital and non-digital media is restricted to authorized users through an approved access control list. Unless guard stations control access to media storage areas, automated mechanisms must be employed to ensure only authorized access to such storage areas, and to audit access attempts and access granted. Currently, the NIST Special Publication 800-53 Rev. 3 does not mandate implementation of this control for low, moderate, or high baseline systems. Therefore, the Census Bureau will not assess any systems according to this control. Program Offices/System Owners may elect to employ cryptographic mechanisms to protect and restrict access to information on portable digital media.

Census Bureau Criteria Program Offices/System Owners must ensure that cryptographic MP-2.3 X mechanisms are employed to protect and restrict access to sensitive information on portable digital media, in accordance with the Census Bureau Acceptable Use Policy. o Census Bureau Acceptable Use Policy Reference http://cww.census.gov/it/itso/docs/2009_Acceptable_Use_Policyv4.0.doc Media Labeling Program Offices/System Owners must ensure that removable information system media and information system output are marked indicating the distribution limitations, handling caveats, and applicable security markings (if any) of the information. The Census Bureau does not exempt any media or hardware component from labeling. Currently, the NIST Special Publication 800-53 Rev. 3 does not mandate implementation of this control for low, moderate, or high baseline systems. Therefore, the Census Bureau will not assess any systems according to this control. Program Offices/System Owners may elect to require that information system media containing classified information are standardized in accordance with NSA standards and policies.

4.11 PHYSICAL AND ENVIRONMENTAL PROTECTION
Class: Operational Physical and environmental security protection measures should be commensurate with the IT resources being protected and the criticality (mission and national security) of the IT resource. The results of a risk assessment and/or a DOC OSY physical security survey help determine the physical security requirements of controlled areas. Physical security refers to the provisions of a safe and secure environment for information processing activities. The Census Bureau OSY has primary responsibility to develop and implement physical security policies, controls, and procedures. The Census Bureau IT Security Office works closely with the Census Bureau OSY to develop policies relevant to IT physical security and to educate employees and contractors on the importance of understanding and abiding by physical security policies at the Census Bureau.
Control Number Security Baselines Control Name/Requirement Low Moderate High

Physical and Environmental Protection Policy and Procedures The Census Bureau IT Security Program Policies document represents the formal documented Census Bureau information security policies, and addresses purpose, scope, roles, responsibilities, and compliance as they pertain to information security Enterprise-level procedural documentation has been developed by ITSO to provide general guidelines for control implementation. The policy and procedures must be reviewed, updated and disseminated at least every other year. Program Offices/System Owners must ensure that: c) A current list of personnel with authorized access to facilities containing information systems (except for areas within the facility officially designated as publicly accessible) is developed and maintained; d) Appropriate authorization credentials (e.g., badges, identification cards, smart cards) are issued; e) The access list and authorization credentials is reviewed and approved at least annually, at which time any personnel no longer requiring access are removed from the access list. Currently, the NIST Special Publication 800-53 Rev. 3 does not mandate implementation of this control for low, moderate, or high baseline systems. Therefore, the Census Bureau will not assess any systems according to this control. Program Offices/System Owners may elect to authorize physical access to facilities where information systems reside based on position or role. Currently, the NIST Special Publication 800-53 Rev. 3 does not mandate implementation of this control for low, moderate, or high baseline systems. Therefore, the Census Bureau will not assess any systems according to this control. Program Offices/System Owners may elect to require two forms of identification to gain access to facilities where information systems reside.

PE-2.3 Program Offices/System Owners may elect to require that physical access to facilities containing information systems that process classified information is restricted to authorized personnel with appropriate clearances and access authorizations. o M-05-24, Implementation of Homeland Security Presidential Directive (HSPD) 12 ­ Policy for a Common Identification Standard for Federal Employees and Contractors ­ Reference http://www.whitehouse.gov/omb/memoranda/fy2005/m05-24.pdf o M-08-01, Homeland Security Presidential Directive 12 (HSPD-12) ­ http://www.whitehouse.gov/omb/memoranda/fy2008/m08-01.pdf Physical Access Control Program Offices/System Owners must ensure that: a) Physical access authorizations are enforced for all physical access points (including designated entry/exit points) to facilities containing information systems (except areas within the facility officially designated as publicly accessible); b) Individual access authorizations are verified before granting access to the facility; c) Entry to facilities containing information systems is controlled using physical access devices and/or guards; d) Access to areas officially designated as publicly accessible is controlled as appropriate (in accordance with the risk assessment conducted); e) Keys, combinations, and other access devices are secured; f) Physical access devices are inventoried at least annually; g) Combinations and keys are changed at least annually and when keys are lost, combinations are compromised, or individuals are transferred or terminated. Physical access authorizations to information systems must be enforced independent of the physical access controls for facilities. An additional layer of physical access security must be provided for areas that are more vulnerable due to a concentration of information system components such as server rooms and communication centers (this does not apply to workstations or peripheral devices dispersed throughout the facility). Therefore, the Census Bureau will not assess any systems according to this control. 4.12 IT SECURITY PLANNING
Class: Management IT security planning is an important quality control tool for the Census Bureau that helps improve the protection level of IT assets. All federal systems have some level of sensitivity and require protection as part of good management practices. The IT security planning process encompasses the following components: Documentation of management, technical, and operational controls in a system's security plan System C&A Security training, awareness, and education. When a management official within the Census Bureau authorizes system operation, the manager accepts the associated risk due to information loss, system misuse, unauthorized system access or modification, system unavailability, and/or undetected system activities. Good security planning, therefore, serves an important risk management function by providing the necessary information to determine the type and level of risks, and to base decisions on risk acceptance or mitigation. Managers must also be assured that all personnel accessing the system, from those performing system management functions to general users, have received security training at levels commensurate with the duties they perform.
Control Number Security Baselines Control Name/Requirement Low Moderate High

Security Planning Policy and Procedures The Census Bureau IT Security Program Policies document represents the formal documented Census Bureau information security policies, and addresses purpose, scope, roles, responsibilities, and compliance as they pertain to information security. Enterprise-level procedural documentation has been developed by ITSO to provide general guidelines for control implementation. The policy and procedures must be reviewed, updated and disseminated at least every other year. DOC Criteria The DOC requires the OUs to inventory all information systems, to include national and non-national security systems using the DOC automated tool. Each OU shall maintain a current inventory for submission to the DOC CISO/SAISO semi-annually (March 15 and September 15).

System Security Plan Program Offices/System Owners must ensure that: a) A security plan is developed for each system (Major Applications (MA) and General Support Systems(GSS)) that: Is consistent with the organization's enterprise architecture; Explicitly defines the authorization boundary for the system; Describes the operational context of the information system in terms of missions and business processes; Provides the security categorization of the information system including supporting rationale; Describes the operational environment for the information system; Describes relationships with or connections to other information systems; Provides an overview of the security requirements for the system; Describes the security controls in place or planned for meeting those requirements (including a rationale for tailoring and supplementation decisions); and Is reviewed and approved by the authorizing official or designated representative prior to plan implementation; b) Security plans for information systems are reviewed annually or upon significant system change; and c) The plan is updated to address changes to information systems/environments of operation or problems identified during plan implementation or security control assessments. Security Related Activity Planning Program Offices/System Owners must plan and coordinate securityrelated activities affecting information systems before conducting such activities in order to reduce the impact on Census Bureau operations (i.e., mission, functions, image, and reputation), Census Bureau assets, and individuals. Routine security-related activities include, but are not limited to, security assessments, audits, system hardware and software maintenance, security certifications, and testing/exercises. 4.13 PERSONNEL SECURITY
Class: Operational Many important issues in computer security involve federal and contractor system users, designers/programmers, implementers/maintainers, and system administrators and managers. A broad range of security issues relates to how these individuals interact with computers and the level of access and authorities they need to do their job. No computer system can be properly secured without properly addressing these security issues.
Control Number Security Baselines Control Name/Requirement Low Moderate High

Personnel Security Policy and Procedures The Census Bureau IT Security Program Policies document represents the formal documented Census Bureau information security policies, and addresses purpose, scope, roles, responsibilities, and compliance as they pertain to information security. Enterprise-level procedural PS-1 documentation has been developed by ITSO to provide general guidelines for control implementation. The policy and procedures must be reviewed, updated and disseminated at least every other year. Position Categorization Program Offices/System Owners must ensure that: a) A risk designation is assigned to all Census Bureau positions; and b) Screening criteria for individuals filling those positions are established; The DOC CISO/SAISO, in coordination with SHRO, OSY, and OAM, reviews and revises position designations on a sampling basis at least annually. DOC Criteria OUs shall comply with the requirements of the DOC Handbook on Suitability and the Department of Commerce Manual of Security Policies and Procedures, which provide criteria for national security positions, and for Low, Medium, and High "risk" non-national security positions. DOC Criteria The CAM Section 1337.70, Security Processing Requirements for OnSite Service Contracts provides contract risk designation criteria and contract language for IT service contracts. (Note: Attachment 1 to CAM 1337.70 has been updated. Please refer to DOC Manual of Security Policies and Procedures, Chapter 10.) In addition, Procurement Memorandum (PM) 2003-09, Information Technology Security Clauses, requires inclusion of CAR 1352.239-74, Security Processing Requirements for Contractor/Subcontractor Personnel for Accessing DOC Information Technology Systems.

4.14 RISK ASSESSMENT
Class: Management As mandated by the DOC, the Census Bureau must have a risk management process in place that follows the methodology and reporting format defined in NIST SP 800-30, Risk Management Guide for Information Technology Systems. Risk management is the ongoing process of managing risks to Census Bureau operations (including mission, functions, image, or reputation), agency assets, or individuals resulting from operating an information system (general support system (GSS) or major application (MA)). It includes assessing risk; selecting, implementing, and assessing cost-effective security controls; and formally authorizing system operation. The process considers effectiveness, efficiency, and constraints due to laws, directives, policies, or regulations. Proper risk management requires steps to be taken to reduce the risk level to an acceptable level. A team led by the system owner and other interested parties first performs a risk assessment for all new systems and systems undergoing major modification. A risk assessment is the methodical identification of (i) threats to a system or information processed or stored by the system, (ii) vulnerability of the system to threats, (iii) probability, or risk, a given threat could exploit the vulnerabilities, and (iv) the effectiveness of current or proposed safeguards/controls. The risk assessment team identifies the controls in place and additional controls needed to provide adequate security for the system and reduces the risk level to one acceptable to the system owner. The system owner then performs periodic vulnerability testing of the controls to monitor the continued adequacy of system security.
Control Number Security Baselines Control Name/Requirement Low Moderate High

Risk Assessment Policy and Procedures The Census Bureau IT Security Program Policies document represents the formal documented Census Bureau information security policies, and addresses purpose, scope, roles, responsibilities, and compliance as they pertain to information security. Enterprise-level procedural documentation has been developed by ITSO to provide general guidelines for control implementation. The policy and procedures must be reviewed, updated and disseminated at least every other year. DOC Criteria The DOC requires the OUs to have a risk management process in place that follows the methodology and reporting format defined by NIST SP 800-30, Risk Management Guide for Information Technology Systems. In addition, if the system uses electronic authentication methods to provide remote access services to citizens, the risk assessment must include an e-authentication risk assessment compliant with OMB M-04-04, E-Authentication Criteria, Attachment A, Section 2.

Security Categorization Program Offices/System Owners must: a) Categorize information systems and the information processed, stored, or transmitted by the systems in accordance with FIPS 199, Standards for Security Categorization of Federal Information and Information Systems and NIST SP 800-60, Guide for Mapping Types of Information and Information Systems to Security Categories, Volume I and II; b) Ensure security categorization results (including supporting rationale) are documented in the system security plan and supporting documentation; and c) Ensure the security categorization decision is reviewed and approved by the authorizing official or authorizing official's designated representative. DOC Criteria DOC deems the following types of information as "non -sensitive": Publicly available information; Non-publicly available information that is derived from publicly available information or that is destined for public dissemination; and, Other information that may not currently be publicly available but that is generally suited for public dissemination (i.e., information whose disclosure would have limited or no adverse effect on organizational operations, organizational assets, or individuals). The term "sensitive" not only refers to unclassified private data or proprietary information, but to highly classified national security government information as well. "Sensitive" information includes any information protected from disclosure by any statute, including the FOIA. DOC Criteria PII refers to information which can be used to distinguish or trace an individual's identity, such as their name, Social Security Number (SSN), biometric records, etc. alone, or when combined with other personal or identifying information which is linked or linkable to a specific individual, such as date and place of birth, mother's maiden name, etc. DOC Criteria The Department requires that SOs follow the methodology defined in NIST SP 800-59, Guideline for Identifying an Information System as a National Security System, to determine whether a system requires additional protections due to national security impacts. o Reference o

Risk Assessment Program Offices/System Owners must: a) Ensure assessments of the risk are conducted, including the likelihood and magnitude of harm, from the unauthorized access, use, disclosure, disruption, modification, or destruction of information systems and the information they process, store, or transmit;. b) Ensure risk assessment results are documented in the risk assessment report; c) Review risk assessment results annually; and d) Ensure the risk assessment is updated annually or whenever there are significant changes to information systems or environments of operation (including the identification of new threats and vulnerabilities), or other conditions that may impact the security state of the system. The system owner may acquire a third party to conduct the assessment, or use in-house personnel. Weakness not readily corrected must be tracked on a system-level POA&M. o

NIST SP 800-30, Risk Management Guide for Information Technology Systems http://csrc.nist.gov/publications/nistpubs/800-30/sp800-30.pdf Vulnerability Scanning Reference Program Offices/System Owners must ensure: a) Scans for vulnerabilities in information systems and hosted applications are conducted at least quarterly and when recommended by the IT Security Office; b) Vulnerability scanning tools are employed that promote interoperability among tools and that automate parts of the vulnerability management process by using standards for: Enumerating platforms, software flaws, and improper configurations; Formatting and making transparent, checklists and test procedures; and Measuring vulnerability impact; c) Vulnerability scan reports and results from security control assessments are analyzed; d) Legitimate high vulnerabilities are remediated within 30 days in accordance with an organizational assessment of risk; and e) Information obtained from the vulnerability scanning process and security control assessments is shared with designated personnel throughout the Census Bureau to help eliminate similar vulnerabilities in other information systems (i.e., systemic weaknesses or deficiencies). Vulnerability scanning tools must include the capability to readily update the list of vulnerabilities. A list of information system vulnerabilities must be maintained and updated quarterly, or when significant new vulnerabilities are identified and reported.

4.15 SYSTEM AND SERVICES ACQUISITION
Class: Management The ITSO, system owners, contracting officers, contracting officer's technical representatives (COTR), and others involved in aspects of system security must follow a methodology consistent with NIST SP 800-64, Security Considerations in the Information System Development Life Cycle. This methodology ensures that IT security is addressed in the acquisition process.
Control Number Security Baselines Control Name/Requirement Low Moderate High

System and Services Acquisition Policy and Procedures The Census Bureau IT Security Program Policies document represents the formal documented Census Bureau information security policies, and addresses purpose, scope, roles, responsibilities, and compliance as they pertain to information security. Enterprise-level procedural documentation has been developed by ITSO to provide general guidelines for control implementation. The policy and procedures must be reviewed, updated and disseminated at least every other year. Program Offices/System Owners must: a) Include a determination of information security requirements for information systems in mission/business planning; b) Determine, allocate, and document resources required to adequately protect information systems as part of their capital planning and investment control process; and c) Establish a discrete line item for information security in Census Bureau programming and budgeting documentation. Allocated resources (including funding) must include all products, procedures, and personnel (federal and contractor) that are primarily dedicated to, or used to provision IT security for the specific IT investment. DOC Criteria All OU CIOs must comply with the DOC capital asset budget planning process and follow a methodology consistent with NIST SP 800-65, Integrating IT Security into the Capital Planning and Capital Investment Control Process. o o Reference o o

Currently, the NIST Special Publication 800-53 Rev. 3 does not mandate implementation of this control for low, moderate, or high baseline systems. Therefore, the Census Bureau will not assess any systems according to this control. NIST SP 800-64, Revision 2, Security Considerations on the System Development Life Cycle http://csrc.nist.gov/publications/nistpubs/800-64-Rev2/SP800-64-Revision2.pdf Developer Security Testing Reference Program Offices/System Owners must ensure that information system developers, in consultation with associated security personnel (including security engineers): a) Create and implement security test and evaluation plans; b) Implement a verifiable flaw remediation process to correct weaknesses and deficiencies identified during the security testing and evaluation process; and c) Document the results of the security testing/evaluation and flaw remediation processes. Developmental security test results may be used to support the security authorization process for the delivered information system, and/or security assessments. Currently, the NIST Special Publication 800-53 Rev. 3 does not mandate implementation of this control for low, moderate, or high baseline systems. Currently, the NIST Special Publication 800-53 Rev. 3 does not mandate implementation of this control for low, moderate, or high baseline systems. Therefore, the Census Bureau will not assess any systems according to this control. Program Offices/System Owners may elect to require that information system developers/integrators perform a vulnerability analysis to document vulnerabilities, exploitation potential, and risk mitigations.

4.16 SYSTEM AND COMMUNICATIONS PROTECTION
Class: Technical The System and Communications Protection control family describes the technical mechanisms that the enterprise can employ to provide a baseline defense against basic system and communication attack methods. The majority of the control mechanisms are designed to be implemented at the server and network tier of the enterprise computing environment; however, selected controls may apply to enterprise applications as well. Common themes, including segmenting computing resources and applying data encryption characterize the system and communications protection control family.
Control Number Security Baselines Control Name/Requirement Low Moderate High

System and Communications Protection Policy and Procedures The Census Bureau IT Security Program Policies document represents the formal documented Census Bureau information security policies, and addresses purpose, scope, roles, responsibilities, and compliance as they pertain to information security. Enterprise-level procedural documentation has been developed by ITSO to provide general guidelines for control implementation. The policy and procedures must be reviewed, updated and disseminated at least every other year. Program Offices/System Owners must ensure information systems either logically and/or physically separate user functionality (including user interface services) from information system management functionality.

SC-6

Boundary Protection Program Offices/System Owners must ensure information systems: a) Monitor and control communications at the external boundaries of information systems and at key internal boundaries within information systems; and b) Connect to external networks or information systems only through managed interfaces consisting of boundary protection devices arranged in accordance with Census Bureau security architecture. Publicly accessible information system components must be physically allocated to separate sub-networks with separate physical network interfaces. The Census Bureau does not allow public access into the Census Bureau internal networks. The number of access points to information systems must be limited to allow for better monitoring of inbound and outbound communications and network traffic.

SC-7.4

Program Offices/System Owners must ensure that: a) A managed interface (boundary protection devices in an effective security architecture) is implemented for each external telecommunication service; b) A traffic flow policy is established for each managed interface; c) Security controls are employed as needed to protect the confidentiality and integrity of information in transmission; d) Each exception to the traffic flow policy is documented with a supporting mission/business need and duration of that need; e) Exceptions to the traffic flow policy are reviewed weekly; and f) Traffic flow policy exceptions that are no longer supported by an explicit mission/business need are removed. Information systems must deny network traffic by default and allow network traffic by exception (i.e., deny all, permit by exception). Program Offices/System Owners must ensure the prevention of unauthorized release of information outside information system boundaries or any unauthorized communication through information system boundaries when there is an operational failure of the boundary protection mechanisms. Information systems must prevent remote devices that have established a non-remote connection with the system from communicating outside of that communications path with resources in external networks. Information systems must route IT traffic destined for the system or application and all external networks through authenticated proxy servers within the managed interfaces of boundary protection devices. Currently, the NIST Special Publication 800-53 Rev. 3 does not mandate implementation of this control for low, moderate, or high baseline systems. NIST SP 800-56A, Revision 1, Recommendation for Pair-Wise Key Establishment Schemes Using Discrete Logarithm Cryptography - http://csrc.nist.gov/publications/nistpubs/80056A/SP800-56A_Revision1_Mar08-2007.pdf Reference o NIST SP 800-57, Recommendation for Key Management http://csrc.nist.gov/publications/nistpubs/800-57/sp800-57-Part1-revised2_Mar08-2007.pdf Use of Cryptography When cryptography is employed within information systems, the Program Office/System Owner must ensure the information system implements cryptographic mechanisms that comply with applicable laws, Executive Orders, directives, policies, regulations, standards, and guidance. The applicable federal standard for employing cryptography in nonnational security information systems is FIPS 140-2 (as amended). Validation certificates issued by the NIST Cryptographic Module Validation Program (including FIPS 140-1, FIPS 140-2, and future amendments) remain in effect and the modules remain available for continued use until a validation certificate is specifically revoked. New purchases and amendments (e.g., additional licenses, cryptographic upgrade) to existing cryptographic modules must be FIPS140-2 compliant. 4.17 SYSTEM AND INFORMATION INTEGRITY
Class: Operational Integrity controls protect data from accidental or malicious alteration or destruction, and ensure users that the quality and reliability of information meets expectations.
Control Number Security Baselines Control Name/Requirement Low Moderate High

System and Information Integrity Policy and Procedures The Census Bureau IT Security Program Policies document represents the formal documented Census Bureau information security policies, and addresses purpose, scope, roles, responsibilities, and compliance as they pertain to information security. Enterprise-level procedural documentation has been developed by ITSO to provide general guidelines for control implementation. The policy and procedures must be reviewed, updated and disseminated at least every other year. Program Offices/System Owners must ensure: a) Information system flaws are identified, reported, and corrected. Security relevant patches, service packs, and hot fixes must be promptly installed. b) Software updates related to flaw remediation are tested for effectiveness and potential side effects on Census Bureau information systems before installation; and c) Flaw remediation is incorporated into the Census Bureau and/or system configuration management processes. The flaw remediation process must be centrally managed and updates installed automatically. Automated mechanisms must be employed to periodically and upon demand determine the state of information system components with regard to flaw remediation. Currently, the NIST Special Publication 800-53 Rev. 3 does not mandate implementation of this control for low, moderate, or high baseline systems. Therefore, the Census Bureau will not assess any systems according to this control. Program Offices/System Owners may elect to require the measurement of the time between flaw identification and flaw remediation and comparison against [Assignment: organization-defined benchmarks]. Currently, the NIST Special Publication 800-53 Rev. 3 does not mandate implementation of this control for low, moderate, or high baseline systems. Therefore, the Census Bureau will not assess any systems according to this control. Program Offices/System Owners may elect to require the employment of automated patch management tools to facilitate flaw remediation to [Assignment: organization-defined information system components]. o NIST SP 800-40, Version 2, Creating a Patch and Vulnerability Management Program http://csrc.nist.gov/publications/nistpubs/800-40-Ver2/SP800-40v2.pdf X

Malicious Code Protection Program Offices/System Owners must ensure that information systems: a) Employ malicious code protection mechanisms at information system entry and exit points and at workstations, servers, or mobile computing devices on the network to detect and eradicate malicious code; Transported by electronic mail, electronic mail attachments, web accesses, removable media, or other common means; or Inserted through the exploitation of information system vulnerabilities; b) Update malicious code protection mechanisms (including signature definitions) whenever new releases are available in accordance with Census Bureau configuration management policy and procedures; c) Configure malicious code protection mechanisms to: Perform periodic scans of the information system weekly and real-time scans of files from external sources as the files are downloaded, opened, or executed in accordance with Census Bureau security policy; and Block malicious code, quarantine malicious code, and/or send an alert to a system administrator in response to malicious code detection; and d) Address the receipt of false positives during malicious code detection and eradication and the resulting potential impact on the availability of the information system. Malicious code protection mechanisms must be managed centrally. Information systems must automatically update malicious code protection mechanisms (including signature definitions). Information systems must prevent non-privileged users from circumventing malicious code protection mechanisms. Currently, the NIST Special Publication 800-53 Rev. 3 does not mandate implementation of this control for low, moderate, or high baseline systems. Therefore, the Census Bureau will not assess any systems according to this control. Program Offices/System Owners may elect to require that information systems update malicious code protection mechanisms only when directed by a privileged user. Currently, the NIST Special Publication 800-53 Rev. 3 does not mandate implementation of this control for low, moderate, or high baseline systems. Therefore, the Census Bureau will not assess any systems according to this control. Program Offices/System Owners may elect to disallow users from introducing removable media into information systems.

NIST SP 800-83, Guide to Malware Incident Prevention and Handling http://csrc.nist.gov/publications/nistpubs/800-83/SP800-83.pdf Information System Monitoring Tools and Techniques Reference Program Offices/System Owners must ensure: a) Events are monitored on information systems using a network-based intrusion detection system (IDS) and system-level IDS, where applicable, to detect information system attacks; b) Unauthorized information system use is identified; c) Monitoring devices are deployed: (i) strategically within information systems to collect essential information; and (ii) at ad hoc locations within information systems to track transactions of interest; d) The level of information system monitoring activity is heightened whenever there is an indication of increased risk to Census Bureau operations and assets, individuals, other organizations, or the Nation based on law enforcement information, intelligence information, or other credible sources of information; and e) Legal opinion with regard to information system monitoring activities is obtained in accordance with application federal laws, Executive Orders, directives, policies, or regulations. All Census Bureau Internet access points must have network-based intrusion detection systems and all Internet-accessible Census Bureau web servers must have host-based intrusion detection systems in place and functioning. Therefore, the Census Bureau will not assess any systems according to this control. Spam Protection Program Offices/System Owners must ensure that: a) Spam protection mechanisms are employed at information system entry and exit points and at workstations, servers, or mobile computing devices on the network to detect and take action on unsolicited messages transported by electronic mail, electronic mail attachments, web accesses, or other common means; and b) Spam protection mechanisms (including signature definitions) are updated when new releases are available in accordance with Census Bureau configuration management policy and procedures. Spam and Spyware protection mechanisms must be centrally managed.

Program Offices/System Owners may elect to require manual initiation of a transfer between active and standby information system component at least once per [Assignment: organization-defined frequency] if the mean time to failure exceeds [Assignment: organization-defined time period].

4.18 PROGRAM MANAGEMENT
The Census Bureau Information Security Program addresses information security requirements for the Census Bureau as a whole, in order to facilitate the management of information security and organizational risks at an enterprise level.
Control Number Security Baselines Control Name/Requirement Low Moderate High

Information Security Program Plan The Census Bureau must: a) Develop and disseminate an Census Bureau-wide information security program plan that: Provides an overview of the requirements for the security program and a description of the security program management controls and common controls in place or planned for meeting those requirements; Provides sufficient information about the program management controls and common controls (including specification of parameters for any assignment and selection operations either explicitly or by reference) to enable an implementation that is unambiguously compliant with the intent of the plan and a determination of the risk to PM-1 be incurred if the plan is implemented as intended; Includes roles, responsibilities, management commitment, coordination among Census Bureau entities, and compliance; Is approved by a senior official with responsibility and accountability for the risk being incurred to Census Bureau operations (including mission, functions, image, and reputation), Census Bureau assets, individuals, other organizations, and the Nation; b) Review the Census Bureau-wide information security program plan annually; and c) Revise the plan to address Census Bureau organizational changes and problems identified during plan implementation or security control assessments. Senior Information Security Officer PM-2 The Census Bureau must appoint a senior agency information security officer (SAISO) with the mission and resources to coordinate, develop, implement, and maintain a Census Bureau-wide information security program.

Appendix B. GLOSSARY
Term Access Control Definition The process of limiting access to the resources of a system only to authorized programs, processes, or other systems (in a network). Synonymous with controlled access and limited access. The official management decision given by a senior agency official to authorize operation of an information system and to explicitly accept the risk to agency operations (including mission, functions, image, or reputation), agency assets, or individuals, based on the implementation of an agreed-upon set of security controls. All components of an information system to be accredited by an Authorizing Official (AO) and excludes separately accredited systems, to which the information system is connected. Synonymous with the term security perimeter defined in CNSS Instruction 4009 and DCID 6/3. The evidence provided to the AO to be used in the security accreditation decision process. Evidence includes, but is not limited to: (i) the System Security Plan; (ii) the assessment results from the security certification; and (iii) the Plan of Action and Milestones (POA&Ms). The independent examination of records and activities to ensure compliance; establish controls, policy, and operational procedures, and to recommend indicated changes in controls, policy, or procedures. A chronological record of system activities that is sufficient to enable the reconstruction, reviewing, and examination of the sequence of environments and activities surrounding or leading to an operation, a procedure, or an event in a transaction from its inception. The authentication mechanism provides an added level of assurance that the user really is who he/she says he/she is. Authentication consists of something a user knows (such as a password), something the user has (such as a token or smart card), or something the user is (such as a fingerprint). It is the process by which the remote user is identified by entering a valid username and password. The AO (or approving/accrediting authority) must be a senior DOC program official or other DOC executive with the authority to take formal responsibility for operating an information system at an acceptable level of risk to agency operations, agency assets, or individuals. An optional role, the AODR is a DOC management employee acting on the AO's behalf in coordinating and carrying out accreditation-related activities required during the security accreditation of an information system. The designated representative interacts with the System Owner (SO), Information System Security Officer, Certification Agent (CA), and other interested parties, and may be empowered by the AO to make decisions with regard to the planning of the C&A activities, including identification of resources necessary to carry out the C&A activities. The granting of access rights to a user, program, or process. The concept that users will be able to access data when needed. A comprehensive assessment of the management, operational and technical security controls in an information system, made in support of security accreditation, to determine the extent to which the controls are implemented correctly, operating as intended, and producing the desired outcome with respect to meeting the security requirements for the system. 158 For Official Use Only

Census Bureau IT Security Policies Term Certification Agent (CA) Confidentiality

April 2010 Definition Also, referred to within DOC as the System Certifier, the CA is an individual, group, or organization responsible for conducting a security certification. The concept of holding sensitive data in confidence, limited to an appropriate set of individuals or organizations. The management of security features and assurances through control of changes made to a system's hardware, software, firmware, documentation, test, test fixtures, and test documentation throughout the development and operational life of the system. A plan for emergency response, back-up operations, and post-disaster recovery maintained by an activity as a part of its security program that will ensure the availability of critical resources and facilitate the continuity of operations in an emergency situation. Synonymous with Emergency Plan, Business Resumption Plan (BRP), and Business Continuity Plan (BCP). An arrangement wherein a third party is contracted by DOC to: 1. Provide IT services and systems on behalf of Commerce at contractor facilities, 2. Provide IT services and systems to Commerce via remote access, and 3. Develop or maintain Commerce IT systems or software. An attack that prevents or impairs the authorized use of networks, systems, or applications by exhausting resources. For example: An attacker sends specially crafted packets to a Web server, causing it to crash. An attacker directs hundreds of external compromised workstations to send as many Internet Control Message Protocol (ICMP) requests as possible to the organization's network. DOC-owned/furnished resources is government equipment including computers, other hardware devices, software, and data that are owned by the DOC and are provided to remote users for use in their official duties. A firewall is a general term for a network perimeter or border router device (may be hardware, software, or both) designed to prevent unauthorized access to or from one networked environment to another networked environment. A computing environment may consist of one or more firewall devices that each protects specific segments of the internal DOC networked environment. The outermost of these devices would face the public Internet. Firewalls can be configured to examine all messages entering or leaving a DOC network and block those messages that are not explicitly allowed by the firewall configuration rules. Forensic examination is the detailed inspection of computer memory and storage media to confirm or deny the occurrence of compromised information and applications, and if compromised, the extent to which information was compromised. A General Support System (GSS) is interconnected information resources under the same direct management control which share common functionality. A GSS normally includes hardware, software, information, data, applications, communications, facilities, and people and provides support for a variety of users and applications.

Census Bureau IT Security Policies Term

April 2010 Definition Occurs when a person violates acceptable computing use policies. For example: A user provides illegal copies of software to others through Peer-to-Peer file sharing services. A person threatens another person through e-mail. The ability to associate positively the identity of a user with the time, method, and degree of access to a system. Information sensitivity reflects the relationship between the characteristics of the information processed (e.g., personnel data subject to protection under the Privacy Act) and the mission need to ensure the confidentiality, integrity, and availability of the information (e.g., legal requirements to protect confidentiality of personal data). Sensitivity may vary from Low, to Moderate, to High. During the system risk assessment, the SO must determine the sensitivity, or reaction, of the agency's mission to compromises of confidentiality, integrity, and availability of the information stored and processed by the system. This determination, along with the likelihood of compromise occurring, establishes the level of security adequate to protect the data as required by OMB Circular A-130, Appendix III. The SO must identify the management, technical, and operational controls necessary to provide the required protection, and properly mark media containing sensitive information. The concept that data, when viewed, will be in sound, unimpaired, or perfect condition. IT resources consist of computer hardware, software, firmware, electronic data, networks, and support for these assets. A discrete set of information resources organized for the collection, processing, maintenance, use, sharing, dissemination, or disposition of information. Computer network that spans a relatively small area, such as a single building or group of buildings. A system that requires special attention to security due to the risk and magnitude of the harm resulting from the loss, misuse, or unauthorized access to or modification of the information in the system. Note: All Federal systems require some level of protection. Certain systems, because of the information in them, however, require special management oversight and should be treated as major. Adequate security for other systems should be provided by security of the systems in which they operate. A virus, worm, Trojan Horse, or other code-based malicious entity that infects a host. For example: A worm uses open file shares to quickly infect several hundred workstations within an organization. An organization receives a warning from an anti-virus vendor that a new virus is spreading rapidly via e-mail throughout the Internet. The virus takes advantage of a vulnerability that is present in many of the organization's hosts. Based on previous anti-virus incidents, the organization expects that the new virus will infect some of its hosts within the next three (3) hours. The security controls (i.e., safeguards or countermeasures) for an information system that focus on the management of risk and the management of information system security. They consist of: risk assessment; planning; system and services acquisition; and certification, accreditation, and security assessment. 160 For Official Use Only

Census Bureau IT Security Policies Term

April 2010 Definition [44 U.S.C., Sec. 3542] Any information system (including any telecommunications system) used or operated by an agency or by a contractor of an agency, or other organization on behalf of an agency-- (i) the function, operation, or use of which involves intelligence activities; involves cryptologic activities related to national security; involves command and control of military forces; involves equipment that is an integral part of a weapon or weapons system; or is critical to the direct fulfillment of military or intelligence missions (excluding a system that is to be used for routine administrative and business applications, for example, payroll, finance, logistics, and personnel management applications); or, (ii) is protected at all times by procedures established for information that have been specifically authorized under criteria established by an Executive Order or an Act of Congress to be kept classified in the interest of national defense or foreign policy. The security controls (i.e., safeguards or countermeasures) for an information system that primarily are implemented and executed by people (as opposed to systems). They consist of: personnel security; physical and environmental protection; contingency planning; configuration management; maintenance; system and information integrity; media protection; incident response; and awareness and training. A protected/private character string used to authenticate an identity. The act of successfully bypassing the security mechanisms of a system. Computers, other hardware devices, and software, owned by the remote access user. The application of physical barriers and control procedures as preventive measures or countermeasures against threats to resources and sensitive information. Computers and other hardware devices owned by a party other than the DOC or the remote user, to which the unrestricted access by the general public is allowed. Access by users (or information systems) communicating external to an information system security perimeter. Remote access uses telecommunications to enable authorized access to non-public DOC computing services that would otherwise be inaccessible from work locations outside a DOC LAN or DOCcontrolled WAN computing environment. This includes access to non-public DOC IT systems and data that are exposed to the public Internet (e.g., Web access to electronic mail by the home user or business traveler) as well as modem dial-up and/or Virtual Private Network (VPN) access to internal DOC IT servers and desktop workstations. A remote location is a work location at which the worker is not able to connect his/her computer directly to a DOC-controlled LAN or DOC-controlled WAN that contains the systems needed for official duties. This includes a worker's home, a traveler's hotel room, or an emergency worker's field location. Work from remote locations requires the use of telecommunications capabilities such as dial-up modems, Internet connectivity, or wireless networks to access DOC IT systems and data for official duty purposes. Any user who requires access to DOC IT systems from a remote location. Users may include DOC federal employees and contractors, employees of other federal agencies who require remote access to DOC systems, and remote researchers processing DOC information. 161 For Official Use Only

Census Bureau IT Security Policies Term Residual Risk Risk

April 2010 Definition The remaining risk not eliminated by implementation of security controls or countermeasures. The probability that a particular threat will exploit a particular vulnerability of the system. The process of identifying risks to agency operations (including mission, functions, image, or reputation), agency assets, or individuals by determining the probability of occurrence, the resulting impact, and additional security controls that would mitigate this impact. Part of risk management, synonymous with risk analysis, and incorporates threat and vulnerability analyses. The process of managing risks to agency operations (including mission, functions, image, or reputation), agency assets, or individuals results from the operation of an information system. It includes risk assessment; cost-benefit analysis; the selection, implementation, and assessment of security controls; and the formal authorization to operate the system. The process considers effectiveness, efficiency, and constraints due to laws, directives, policies, or regulations. Process to remove information from media such that information recovery is not possible. It includes removing all labels, markings, and activity logs. An evaluation done to assess the degree of trust that can be placed in systems for the secure handling of sensitive information. One type, a product evaluation, is an evaluation performed on the hardware and software features and assurances of a computer product from a perspective that excludes the system environment. The other type, a system evaluation, is done for the purpose of assessing a system's security safeguards with respect to a specific operational mission and is a major step in the certification and accreditation (C&A) process. The security-relevant functions, mechanisms, and characteristics of system hardware and software. Security features are a subset of system security safeguards. The set of laws, rules, and practices that regulate how an organization manages, protects, and distributes sensitive information. The types and levels of protection necessary for equipment, data, information, software applications, and facilities to meet security policy. The protective measures and controls that are prescribed to meet the security requirements specified for a system. Those safeguards may include, but are not necessarily limited to: hardware and software security features, operating procedures, accountability procedures, access and distribution controls, management constraints, personnel security, and physical structures, areas, and devices. Also called safeguards. ST&E is the process used to examine the effectiveness of IT system controls with the objective of determining the true risk, or exposure, of the system to certain threats. Through the conduct of control tests, the ITSO and SO identify vulnerabilities that result from improper use of controls, missing controls, inherent system vulnerabilities, or mismanagement. Through the application of ST&E methods, the CA analyzes the current state of the system by reviewing the system objects, and searching for anomalies that might indicate vulnerabilities that could permit an attack. ST&E results in development of a POA&Ms to track corrective actions necessary to mitigate vulnerabilities and reduce risk. 162 For Official Use Only
